[{"id":35304,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/2018-19-kia-rookie-ladder-week-16","date":"2019-02-28","title":"Kia Rookie Ladder: Young, Bagley putting pressure on Doncic","content":" Luka Doncic has grabbed the hearts of NBA fans, but if he thinks the second half is going to be a cakewalk to a Kia Rookie of the Year trophy, he better think again. He\u2019s got some company at the top. After struggling to start the season, Atlanta Hawks point guard Trae Young is playing fantastic basketball of late. While early indications had some prognosticators wondering how he\u2019d ever fit in the NBA, his recent play has him looking like a future star. Since the All-Star break , Young has topped 30 points in three of four games, with back-to-back 36-point games. Young shot just 19.8 percent from 3-point land in November, but he\u2019s been constantly improving from deep since then. In Sacramento, Marvin Bagley III has seen his playing time increase, and fans are seeing a franchise cornerstone and perennial All-Star. Before Wednesday\u2019s game \u2014 which he left after spraining his knee in the third quarter \u2014 Bagley was averaging 24 points, 11.7 rebounds and 1.7 blocks in the first three games since the All-Star break . He had three straight double-doubles, including a 28-point, 14-rebound showing against the defending-champion Golden State Warriors . Deandre Ayton, who had been the biggest competition for Doncic through the first half, is still lingering, but his numbers have dropped off enough to require a serious uptick to make a run at Doncic. Will anyone be able to catch Doncic? It might take a miracle, but Young and Bagley (assuming his injury isn\u2019t serious) are going to make him earn it. * * * Last week:  No. 1 Doncic missed the first two games after the All-Star break with a sore right ankle, but returned with a pair of respectable games. Doncic put up a triple-double in Dallas\u2019 121-112 loss to the LA Clippers with 28 points, 10 rebounds and 10 assists. He then followed that up by leading the Mavs to a 110-101 win over the Pacers with another big game. He put up 26 points, 10 rebounds and seven assists and hit a clutch 3-pointer in the final minute to seal the win. The only negative for Doncic has been the 16 turnovers in the last two games \u2013 nine in L.A. followed by seven vs. the Pacers. Last week:  No. 2 As mentioned above, Young might be the only rookie with a chance to catch Doncic, who has likely already won over many voters with his consistent play. But looking at his numbers from February , you can start to see Young is gaining on Doncic to make a case. For the month, Doncic finishes with averages of 24.4 ppg, 9.4 rpg, 7.4 apg while shooting 44.3 percent overall (and 36.2 percent on 3-pointers). Young\u2019s numbers? Try 23.3 ppg, 4.3 rpg, 9.3 apg while shooting 41.0 percent overall (and 43.7 percent 3-pointers). Not much of a separation there, and Young \u2014 coming off back-to-back 36-point games \u2014 is certainly looking like he\u2019s ready to make a run at Doncic\u2019s top spot. Last week:  No. 4 Bagley is due to have an MRI on Thursday for what the team called a sprained left knee, which is terrible news considering just how dominant Bagley has been lately. The No. 2 pick got a rare start on Monday, going toe-to-toe with Karl-Anthony Towns with 25 points, 11 rebounds and a pair of blocks in 37 minutes. Bagley\u2019s been big for the Kings off the bench all season, but it\u2019s clear his time has come and \u2014 if the injury doesn\u2019t turn out to be serious \u2014 the Kings\u2019 playoff hopes hinge on his continued emergence down the stretch. Last week:  Not ranked The Knicks\u2019 rookie has turned into quite the sensation, capturing the hearts of fans at Madison Square Garden. The Knicks won back-to-back games this week, and Robinson was a major factor in both victories. In the Knicks\u2019 against San Antonio on Sunday, Robinson put up 15 points, 14 rebounds and five blocks to help New York snap an 18-game home losing streak. Two nights later, the 7-foot-1 center had 17 points, 14 rebounds, six blocks and three steals in New York\u2019s comeback win vs. Orlando . Robinson became the third rookie in the last 25 years to tally a double-double with at least five blocks in back-to-back games. The other two? Hall of Famer Yao Ming and future Hall of Famer Tim Duncan. The two wins brought attention to the energetic rookie, but he\u2019s been solid all month (10.9 ppg, 8.9 rpg, 3.3 bpg in 22.6 mpg off the bench). Last week:  No. 3 Ayton has seen his numbers dip since the All-Star break , but here\u2019s the thing: They\u2019re still pretty good. In three games, Ayton averaged 13.7 ppg, 10.3 rpg and 1.3 spg, but he was -14.3 in plus\/minus as the Suns went 1-2. That lone win, of course, came just a few days after Ayton promised he was ready to \u201ctake over\u201d and the Suns snapped their 17-game losing streak with a win against the Miami Heat. It will be interesting to see how the Suns handle Ayton down the stretch, and it would be nice to see the team actually run plays for their prize big man and let him \u201ctake over\u201d as he\u2019s promised. Allonzo Trier, New York Knicks Trier has been big in the Knicks\u2019 three games since the All-Star break , averaging 15.7 ppg on 53.8 percent shooting. His most notable performance came in the Knicks\u2019 win over the Magic, in which he scored 18 points, grabbed five rebounds and had three steals in 21 minutes. Josh Okogie, Minnesota Timberwolves In the four games since the All-Star break , the Wolves\u2019 lock-down defender has averaged 2.3 steals, thanks in large part to a four-steal game in a big win against the Kings. Okogie continues to be one of this class\u2019 best defenders Jalen Brunson, Dallas Mavericks The Mavs\u2019 other rookie guard is proving he belongs, and he had his best game Wednesday in Dallas\u2019 110-101 win against Indiana . Brunson started and scored a career-high 24 points\u2019 on 9-for-14 shooting, hitting 3 of 6 3-pointers, including a clutch one in the final minute. \u201cI\u2019m there to help keep the energy,\u201d said Brunson, who is averaging 16.8 points in the four games since the All-Star break . \u201cObviously Luka means a lot to this team, but I try to play pickup defense and stay available for my teammates. I\u2019m there to play hard.\u201d Jaren Jackson Jr., Memphis Grizzlies Jackson deserves a mention solely because he\u2019s been a fixture around here. However, Nowitzki never officially ruled out a return for season No. 22 and seems to be pondering that notion of late. Nowitzki started in last night\u2019s 110-101 home win against the Indiana Pacers, which marked his third straight start. He finished with 11 points, five rebounds and three assists, hitting a key 3-pointer early in the fourth quarter to help keep the Pacers at bay. The game was his first home start this season and afterward, Nowitzki said he\u2019s feeling better of late. When asked if his recent surge in playing time and role has shaped his thoughts on the future, Nowitzki did not commit to an answer. But, he also didn\u2019t deny the possibility of an NBA-record 22nd season come 2019-20. \u201cI don\u2019t know,\u201d he said, per Brad Townsend of the Dallas Morning News . \u201cI haven\u2019t really thought about it. I would love to be there for the young guys one more year, but I think it depends on how the body feels. I\u2019ve had issues obviously this year. I had some knee swelling here the last few weeks, actually before the All-Star break, so it\u2019s not all great. But like I said I am feeling better. I am feeling stronger. But I think I\u2019m going to make that decision later on.\u201d Playing along side rookie phenom Luka Doncic as well as newly acquired former All-Star forward Kristaps Porzingis seems to entice Nowitzki as well. \u201cI think Luka and KP, if they stay healthy, stay together, they should be a great combo,\u201d Nowitzki said, per ESPN\u2019s Tim MacMahon . \u201cThey should play great off each other. Both have an incredible skill set for their size, incredible playmaking ability for their size. They should jell well, but we have to see how it goes next year.\u201d Nowitzki, 40, missed the first 26 games of this season while he recovered from an inflamed tendon in his left foot. Since his return \u2014 which came on Dec. 13 vs. Phoenix \u2014 he played 16 minutes or less in 23 of his 25 games (including multiple games of 10 minutes or less). However, he has seen a big uptick in minutes of late, logging 17 or more minutes in six of his last eight games. He played 22 minutes last night, which came after logging 26 minutes in a Feb. 25 loss to the LA Clippers and 25 minutes in a Feb. 23 loss to the Utah Jazz . Nowitzki has scored 11 or more points in four of his last five games and is 69 points away from passing Wilt Chamberlain for sixth on the NBA\u2019s all-time scoring list. \u201cI feel like I have a little more pep in my step,\u201d Nowitzki said, per ESPN. \u201cMy legs and my wind are a lot better than [earlier in the season]. I just feel better overall. I feel like I can actually contribute, whereas earlier I was struggling just to get up and down.\u201d To open the season, Nowitzki spent most of it coming off the bench \u2014 in large part to accommodate playing time for center DeAndre Jordan. In acquiring Porzingis from the New York Knicks , though, the Mavs dealt Jordan \u2014 which opened up some more playing time for Nowitzki. Per ESPN, Porzingis has quietly lobbied for Nowitzki to return for season No. 22, as the youngster has long been a fan of Nowitzki\u2019s game and wants to play with him. Nowitzki, who led the Mavericks to their only championship as the NBA Finals MVP in 2011, took pride in playing 77 games last season as a 39-year-old. He hoped for a similar number in what could be his final season. Instead, it\u2019s been more like 2012-13, when he missed 27 games after preseason arthroscopic surgery on his right knee. The highest-scoring foreign-born player, Nowitzki is sixth on the career list with 31,351 points. He was sixth to start the season before LeBron James passed him early. James is up to fifth and is just 98 points from passing Michael Jordan for the No. 4 all-time spot. Information from The Associated Press was used in this report."},{"id":35301,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/about-last-night-2-27-19","date":"2019-02-28","title":"About Last Night: Buzzer-beater by a winner","content":" In a title-winning career filled with big moments, Dwyane Wade notched another one Wednesday night. We don\u2019t know whether Wade\u2019s wild 3-point buzzer-beater to lift the Miami Heat over the reigning champion Golden State Warriors 126-125 is a career capstone. Although this is Wade\u2019s 16th and final season, who knows, bigger moments might remain in the Heat\u2019s 22 remaining regular-season games as they battle for a playoff berth. But this one was certainly joyous, memorable and something of a rarity \u2014 evoking a 10-year-old fumbled buzzer-beater by Devin Harris. The home crowd lavished applause on the hometown hero after Wade\u2019s off-balance shot banked in as time expired. \u201cWe just kept fighting and kept believing,\u201d Wade said on-court during a walkoff interview during which he heaped praise on Kevin Durant, who made some big shots and finished with 29 points. \u201cThe ball bobbled around and everything and I just got it and tried to put it up. The Good Lord put it in. I\u2019m just overwhelmed right now.\u201d It was the fifth \u2014 and quite possibly the final \u2014 game-winning buzzer-beater of Wade\u2019s career. As always, we rate game-winning buzzer-beaters on our Horry Scale. Reminder: The Horry Scale breaks down a game-winning buzzer-beater (GWBB) in the categories of difficulty, game situation (was the team tied or behind at the time?), importance (playoff game or garden-variety night in January?) and celebration. Then we give it an overall grade on a scale of 1-5 Robert Horrys, named for the patron saint of last-second answered prayers. *** DIFFICULTY: This was a 3-pointer, but not a long-distance 3. And Wade appeared to have a good look at the top of the key after receiving a pass from Dion Waiters. But Jordan Bell closed quickly and partially blocked it, knocking it out of Wade\u2019s hands. Twisting to regain control, Wade grabbed it and tossed it toward the basket off of one leg \u2014 a difficult move for an improbable off-the-glass bank shot as time expired. GAME SITUATION:  The Heat let a 24-point lead slip away, and were fighting mightily to rally from a four-point deficit in the final minute. This was a game the Heat, losers of seven of their last 10, needed to keep place in the hunt for the No. 8 playoff spot in the East. The wild sequence began with 10 seconds left and the Heat trailing by two. Wade dribbled up court, almost lost the ball but regained it, and found Waiters who returned it to Wade with about 2.5 seconds remaining. That\u2019s when Wade tried to shoot the 3, was blocked and regained it for the wild heave as time expired. The looks of disbelief on the Warriors said it all. CELEBRATION: The Heat didn\u2019t punch their ticket to The Finals, but you would have thought so from the celebration. Wade ran the length of the court while the crowd roared and his teammates caught up and mobbed him. He then mounted a courtside table and pounded his chest three times before taking a victory lap while waving a white towel. GRADE: The only thing keeping this from being the highest grade \u2014 five Horrys \u2014 is that it won a game with relatively little on the line. 4 1\/2 Horrys .  Celtics fall again  The Boston Celtics remain winless since the All-Star break, having lost four in a row. The latest came at the hands of the Portland Trail Blazers, who are now riding a five-game winning streak. The Blazers, behind Damian Lillard\u2019s 33 points, held off the Celtics 97-92 , after outscoring them by 11 in the third quarter. Boston played with more energy tonight but things still didn\u2019t go its way. Kyrie Irving scored 31 points in the loss. He may be 42, but the Hawks\u2019 Vince Carter still has hops and he can hang with the best. Watch him defy gravity to drop in a one-handed 2-pointer on the way down over the Wolves\u2019 Karl-Anthony Towns. He also took a forearm in the abdomen. It wasn\u2019t pretty, but James Harden scored 30 points in his first game after his 32-game streak of 30-plus points was broken on Monday night vs. the Hawks. And while 30 is nothing to sneeze at for the average player, it\u2019s a mediocre day for Harden, who scored 50-plus four times during the streak. But now he\u2019s struggling with his long-distance shooting. Still, the Rockets are winning while Harden is a bit off his lofty standards, taking down the Hawks on Monday and pulling ahead of the Charlotte Hornets in the fourth quarter to hold on for a 118-113 win . Harden\u2019s performance from the line (9-for-9) down the stretch and PJ Tucker\u2019s 3-point shooting (5-for-5) gave the Rockets the win. Amazingly, Harden was 0-for-22 from beyond the arc spanning three games before nailing a 3-pointer with 3:19 left in the third quarter. He finished the night 1-of-11 from long distance after going 0-10 on Monday, when the scoring streak ended. Being off on the 3 can hurt, as this sequence shows. With seconds left in the third quarter, Marvin Williams takes an outlet pass off the rebound from Harden\u2019s clanger, dribbles a time or two and heaves a shot from 6 feet inside the half-court line to beat the buzzer. It was a six-point turnaround that gave Charlotte a 94-90 lead entering the fourth. Though Charlotte couldn\u2019t close out Houston, Kemba Walker finished with 35 points in the Hornets\u2019 loss after pouring in 18 in the second quarter and 27 in the first half. Anthony Davis\u2019 look said it all. LeBron James showed again how he makes a big shot down the stretch to put away an opponent \u2014 this time the New Orleans Pelicans. The dagger came with about 31 seconds left and the shot clock winding down as the Lakers clung to a 120-117 lead. James lost the handle against Julius Randle, regained it and dribbled to the corner where he fired an off-balance 3-point shot that touched nothing but net as the shot clock expired. With a six-point lead and the Pelicans deflated, the Lakers held on to win 125-119 . It marked a much-needed win for the Lakers, who are in danger of falling out of the playoff hunt in power-packed Western Conference. The Milwaukee Bucks edged the Sacramento Kings 141-140 in overtime , and the loss may have been costly for the Kings. Marvin Bagley III went down near the end of the third quarter and writhed in pain before being helped off. After the game, the Kings called the injury a knee sprain and said Bagley would undergo an MRI on Thursday to determine the extent of the damage. A talented and lucky fan drained a half-court shot at halftime of the New Orleans Pelicans at Los Angeles Lakers contest to bag a cool $100K. Arguably, Dean Tran of Camarillo, California, has more reason to be happy about his shot than Wade was about his buzzer-beater. The 40-year-old becomes the eighth winner, aside from ex-Laker Vlade Divac, who shot for charity, to win the MGM Big Shot Jackpot, a promotion which began during the 2006-07 season. Tran is the second MGM Big Shot Jackpot winner of the season, and first since Ali Sabbouri of Anaheim, California won $30,000 on October 22, 2018. Not Evan Turner."},{"id":35299,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/pelicans-peculiar-ad-situation-reaches-pivot","date":"2019-02-28","title":"Pelicans' peculiar situation with Davis reaches a pivot point","content":" LOS ANGELES \u2014 They represent a city that takes pride in being quirky, mysterious and wonderfully peculiar \u2014 although none of these traits quite make sense for basketball. The New Orleans Pelicans are different than most NBA teams right now, that\u2019s for sure, and not for all the right reasons. The Pelicans are caught in the crossroads as the regular season begins its lurch toward the end, dropping Wednesday\u2019s game to the Los Angeles Lakers, 125-119. New Orleans\u2019 best player, a top-five NBA talent, doesn\u2019t want to be there. They can\u2019t \u2014 or either won\u2019t \u2014 play him more than 20 or so minutes a night, if he plays at all. The Pelicans are headed for a losing season, there\u2019s a long-term vacancy at general manager, questions about ownership exist, and there are limited assets on the roster to create a drastic makeover. These are not normal or healthy signs for an NBA team, and potentially troublesome for one located in a small market. Yet the Pelicans have no choice but to steer the rocky ship until solutions can be found in the offseason, starting with what to do with Anthony Davis. The team and the player are trying to make the best of an uncomfortable (though not unprecedented) situation. Last month, when Davis informed the Pelicans through his agency (which also represents LeBron James) that he wanted to be traded , neither side imagined they\u2019d be in this situation heading into March: stuck with each other for another two months. Yet, here they are. \u201cWe had discussions and this is what we\u2019re doing,\u201d said Davis, referencing an arrangement that has him on a minutes restriction, mainly to protect him and the team. If Davis gets injured, that could affect his trade value this summer, which serves no one any good \u2014 not him, not the Pelicans and not any team interested in acquiring him. Also, the league frowns upon healthy players being stashed at home, especially if they\u2019re considered box-office types, so everyone\u2019s satisfied with Davis in uniform \u2026 sort of. In truth, the Pelicans and Davis can\u2019t wait for this season to end. It\u2019s not an especially good look, both sides putting on a good face through a tough situation. The Pelicans have begun plans for life after Davis, except there\u2019s no permanent general manager in place yet, with Danny Ferry serving in the interim since the firing of Dell Demps two weeks ago. Whomever gets the job must bring sturdy boots and rolled-up sleeves. This will be a chore, and the Pelicans can\u2019t afford to miss. That means the Draft (where they\u2019ll likely select a lottery pick), in any trade proposal for Davis, and in deciding what, if anything, to do with coach Alvin Gentry (whose status beyond this season is also unclear). A series of bad moves could put the franchise in peril. The Pelicans aren\u2019t considered a destination for A-list free agents \u2014 and their franchise player wants out, which raises red flags \u2014 making it imperative that they avoid big mistakes. That could have a rippling effect on a team that isn\u2019t exactly one of the league\u2019s big earners and already dealing with the perception that ownership, which also owns the NFL\u2019s New Orleans Saints, leans football. Gayle Benson, widow of Tom Benson, now controls the Pelicans and in her statement announcing the dismissal of Demps, she dismissed any notion of the basketball team as a lower priority. She used strong words \u2014 \u201cI am prepared to provide any and all resources to compete for championships\u201d \u2014 to reassure wavering fans about the immediate and long-term future of the club. Proof is in the production, however, and Benson\u2019s pledge will be tested by the upcoming decisions that will help or hurt the reshaping of the team. With the right move, the Davis trade could greatly help put bounce in the franchise. They could try to follow the same manner as the Indiana Pacers did in trading Paul George (and Indiana wasn\u2019t holding great leverage in its trade with Oklahoma City). Once the Draft order is determined in on May 14, teams holding lottery picks will begin putting together packages for Davis. A savvy GM will essentially hold an auction and use the incoming assets to keep or deal for players who can refresh the team and build toward the future. There\u2019s an urgency to draft correctly and find young players to develop and maybe even draft the next \u2026 Davis? Their costly blunder, and the reason they\u2019re in this situation, was a failure to maximize Davis\u2019 prime years. Crummy luck with injuries have also doomed the Pelicans the last four seasons, with none more damaging than DeMarcus Cousins rupturing his Achilles\u2019 tendon 13 months ago. To get Cousins from the Kings, the Pelicans dealt Buddy Hield, now a deadly shooter who might be reaching the All-Star fringes. Cousins, meanwhile, has since joined the Warriors, meaning the Pelicans have zilch to show for the trade. Each big face-palm, especially with a lottery selection, can set a team back a few years. After winning only one playoff series with Davis, the Pelicans can\u2019t afford to start from the bottom again, or else risk the sight of empty sections throughout their arena. In the meantime, there\u2019s a season to be played between now and any potential deal, a season that doesn\u2019t seem to serve much purpose with Davis simply biding his time and only halfway invested. \u201cWe just have to continue to play basketball,\u201d said Gentry, sounding trapped and resigned to this fate. \u201cAt the end of the day, that\u2019s all we can do.\u201d * * * Shaun Powell has covered the NBA for more than 25 years. "},{"id":35278,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/ap-bucks-kings-social-injustice-initiative","date":"2019-02-28","title":"Bucks, Kings collaborate to address social injustice","content":" SACRAMENTO, Calif. (AP) \u2014 Nearly a year after police fatally shot an unarmed black man in Sacramento and a series of protests ensued in California\u2019s capital, the Kings and Milwaukee Bucks collaborated on a daylong summit Wednesday to address social injustice and encourage engagement and thoughtful discussions to try to bring about change. The event held ahead of a Bucks-Kings game came nearly a year after the March 18, 2018, fatal shooting of 22-year-old Stephon Clark. Clark\u2019s death ignited a series of protests that included protesters joining hands and blocking entrances to the Kings\u2019 downtown arena as owner Vivek Ranadive pledged his support and vowed to do his part to address the issue. \u201cI made a commitment that we would work hard to have an impact and do better and bring people together,\u201d Ranadive said Wednesday. Ranadive was joined by Milwaukee co-owner Marc Lasry for a panel discussion along with Mark Thomsen, the attorney for Bucks guard Sterling Brown. The Bucks were rocked last year when Brown, then a rookie, was Tased by police. He later filed a lawsuit saying the officers\u2019 use of a stun gun during his arrest for a parking violation constituted excessive force and that they targeted him because he is black. Both owners hope further awareness might encourage more teams and communities to get on board to have a dialogue about issues and create positive change. \u201cI hope this concept goes viral,\u201d Ranadive said. Brown said he appreciated the efforts by both organizations. \u201cWhenever the team can do something as big as this for the community, it\u2019s important,\u201d Brown said after the Bucks\u2019 morning shootaround. \u201cIt definitely lets some of the community members know that it is a push to make change, especially for myself, I\u2019m pretty big on that where I stand and my situation and the platform I have. I\u2019m looking to make significant changes in the community to help the urban, the black community progress.\u201d Brown had been talking with officers while waiting for a citation for illegally parking in a disabled spot outside a Walgreens at about 2 a.m. on Jan. 26, 2018, when officers took him down because he didn\u2019t immediately remove his hands from his pockets as ordered. An officer yelled: \u201cTaser! Taser! Taser!\u201d Brown later received a formal apology from the city\u2019s police chief. \u201cI knew Sterling and it didn\u2019t sound like him,\u201d Lasry said. \u201cSterling, in my opinion, was just a great kid. And it didn\u2019t make sense, it didn\u2019t sound like him. \u2026 As we got more information we sort of came to a crossroads, which is there\u2019s Sterling\u2019s side and there was the other side. For us an organization we ended up coming down on Sterling\u2019s side simply because we knew him as a person.\u201d Thomsen credited the Bucks for backing his client from the very start. He said he is pushing for Milwaukee\u2019s police department to use this case as training. \u201cYou can\u2019t heal until there is accountability,\u201d Thomsen said. After Clark\u2019s death in California, Ranadive made an impassioned pledge of support for the protesters and the community at large following the first round of demonstrations on March 22 after first consulting with his players. Ranadive, the first person of Indian descent to own an NBA franchise, said after a game last year, \u201cWe stand here before you, old, young, black, white, brown, and we are all united in our commitment.\u201d Ranadive said the efforts remain a work in progress and he is striving for every kid in the community \u201cto have a voice.\u201d \u201cI\u2019ve always felt this is bigger than basketball,\u201d Ranadive reiterated Wednesday. \u201d\u2026 At the end of the day we have to take actions, and actions speak louder than words.\u201d"},{"id":35276,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/warriors-stoneman-douglas-kids","date":"2019-02-27","title":"Warriors host kids from Stoneman Douglas at practice","content":"MIAMI (AP) \u2014 Stephen Curry would ordinarily be getting off his feet as fast as possible after a morning shootaround practice, saving his legs for the looming game that night.  Wednesday, however, wasn\u2019t ordinary.  Golden State coach Steve Kerr invited some students \u2014 including ones from Marjory Stoneman Douglas High, the school in Parkland where 17 students and staff were killed in a massacre on Feb. 14, 2018 \u2014 into the Warriors\u2019 game-morning practice in Miami. And long after the session was over, Curry was throwing alley-oop lobs and engaging in 3-point contests with kids who couldn\u2019t believe they were hanging out with stars from the two-time defending NBA champions.  \u201cYou hate that you have these opportunities because of what happened at our school,\u201d said Jeff Foster, a teacher and former coach at Stoneman Douglas. \u201cBut at the same time, it\u2019s nice to have these contacts and meet people and coach Kerr has been at a few of the events with our kids \u2026 you\u2019re always glad to sit around and talk to him, whether it\u2019s about basketball or politics. And we just spent time doing both.\u201d     While Kerr was chatting with teachers, some of the boys and girls got onto the court with the Warriors. Andre Iguodala, Shaun Livingston, Kevin Durant and Curry were among those who stuck around after shootaround for about an extra half-hour, posing for photos and talking about basketball.  \u201cIt\u2019s special having them here,\u201d Curry said as he watched the kids playing on the same court where the Warriors would visit the Miami Heat on Wednesday night. \u201cThey\u2019ve done so much in the wake of the shooting, speaking out, using their platform that they have, the entire student body. They come to just have fun, enjoy themselves. I know that means a lot.\u201d  Matt Fisher won\u2019t forget it anytime soon.  Fisher is among the captains of Marjory Stoneman Douglas\u2019 boys team, which lost its district championship game in quadruple-overtime and then fell in the first round of the state tournament. Good decision?  * * * Steve Aschburner :  Many professions, especially those that collectively bargain with labor, set thresholds and qualifications for entry, so let\u2019s dispense with any right-to-work histrionics, OK? For the NBA\u2019s sake, I\u2019d prefer to see the age go up rather than down , so that the players we see are more developed and ready to help their teams. But the league owes nothing to the NCAA, and if the G League can function as a proper affiliate system across all 30 NBA franchises \u2013 and only the rare precocious stars leapfrog legit farm-system seasoning \u2013 then there\u2019s no reason players can\u2019t learn in Erie, Pa., and Schaumburg, Ill., rather than Durham, N.C., and Lexington, Ky. Shaun Powell :  I think lowering the age limit only helps maybe two or three players. That\u2019s it. Yes, a Zion Williamson can go straight to the pros because obviously he has an NBA body already and a decent game. But it also puts a strain on NBA GMs and scouting. Coming to a high school gym near you: Dozens of NBA scouts! John Schuhmann :  Yes. It\u2019s silly to have an 18-year-old go to college just to play basketball for one season and (in some cases) leave to prepare for the Draft before the spring semester is even over. Some players will make mistakes by skipping school and it will be tougher for both players and teams to evaluate how they measure up within the potential Draft class (a mix of high school and college players). But the improved and expanded G League offers a safer landing spot than what was in place prior to 2006.  Sekou Smith :  No-brainer decision.  And certainly from where I\u2019m sitting, it\u2019s a good decision. Folks will debate the merits for and against 18 or 19 for years to come. I\u2019m just a believer that anything past a player\u2019s 18th birthday is a rule that goes against everything this country is about (yes, I\u2019m taking it there.). The same choice kids make to attend college should include the option of bypassing the college game altogether for the professional option, be it in the NBA or anywhere else. The star player becomes a flashpoint for the boiling frustration, and they scramble to find elusive solutions as the season begins to pass them by. And, get this: The main role can be played by \u2026 wait for it \u2026 LeBron himself! Hollywood loves nothing more than a deliciously dramatic reality show, and how convenient is it that one is unspooling right before LeBron\u2019s very eyes, or shall we say, very weary and confused eyes? Just as he wields power over his growing entertainment empire, he\u2019s also mainly responsible for the situation buckling the Lakers as they stumble and flail and threaten to crumble during this stretch run toward the playoffs . Should they blow this chance \u2014 and it\u2019s getting slippery by the game \u2014 it would be a rude gut-punch, though not a damaging one, to LeBron\u2019s legacy, which he cares so deeply about. It would raise questions moving forward about his leadership style, his curious link to the player agency he helped form, his degree of power within the Lakers (and whether it\u2019s too expansive). And, most importantly, it would raise questions about his ability to attract A-list free agents before either his contract runs out or Father Time taps him on the shoulder. At the moment, the Lakers are broken, far from what team president Magic Johnson and LeBron and others projected upon signing last summer. Where do we start? A number of teammates, according to those close to them, resented LeBron\u2019s role in the Anthony Davis chase \u2014 when half the rotation was ready to be shipped to New Orleans \u2014 and also his comments after the All-Star break, when LeBron seemed to blame everyone but himself for embarrassing losses to the Pelicans and Grizzlies. Most of the locker room held great admiration for LeBron before the season began, and how could they not? But the mood is shifting \u2026 and how could it not? LeBron\u2019s also playing for a coach who \u2014 if the whispers are true \u2014 he doesn\u2019t totally endorse. So, how do you expect Luke Walton to feel? LeBron\u2019s play since returning from his groin injury hasn\u2019t been stellar, with notable defensive lapses, which perhaps could be blamed on age and LeBron\u2019s tendency in the past to pick his spots on when to play both ends of the floor. He could get away with that when his teams in Cleveland and Miami won. That\u2019s not so true now. Given all that, some perspective is needed and should be heard through the noise of the past few days. The Lakers simply wouldn\u2019t be in this position if LeBron didn\u2019t miss a month. Also, Lonzo Ball, who was developing nicely before twisting an ankle, still hasn\u2019t returned. Poor defense, turnovers and misfires from the free throw line are team-wide problems, not just a LeBron problem. Besides, even on his worst days, LeBron is more productive and consistent and far beyond the next best Laker, whoever that is. Finally, there is this: This was always designated as a bridge year with a still-maturing young core that needed seasoning and vets on one-year contracts. But of course, LeBron is being paid and treated as a savior, and making the playoffs was supposed to be a given. Plus, some of the Lakers\u2019 losses have been downright shameful. The Davis drama, which seemed to have LeBron\u2019s fingerprints all over it, not only hasn\u2019t helped matters, but also caused plenty of grief and distrust among his teammates. Does LeBron have their backs, or is he trying to shove a knife in them? Because of his obvious clout, not a single player will confront LeBron for answers about where they stand. They\u2019re either too young and intimidated, or too old and deep into their careers and don\u2019t want to jeopardize any chances of getting an extension. This is a different climate for LeBron. He was held in high regard in Cleveland and Miami locker rooms. He was the superstar who always and willingly shared his off-the-court riches with teammates \u2014 gifting them designer headphones, expensive cell phones and anything else he hawked. When they went out with him socially, they could count on automatic entry beyond doors closed to most people. It was good to be teammates with LeBron. He took care of them, looked out for them, elevated them. And now? Given what is transpiring with the Lakers, his current teammates probably shouldn\u2019t expect any cameos in \u201cSpace Jam 2.\u201d It\u2019s also a case study in the power LeBron has within the Lakers. He\u2019s more or less partners with Magic, a relationship he didn\u2019t have with Pat Riley in Miami \u2014 Riles drew the line more than once with LeBron \u2014 and not to this extent in Cleveland. That kind of power and voice within the organization doesn\u2019t go unnoticed among teammates. Suppose, for example, the Lakers strike out on trading for Davis this summer. Can you imagine the handful of players dangled in that trade returning to the team next season, willing and anxious to forgive and forget? There is a temporary fix. The Lakers can start winning, starting with Wednesday\u2019s game against the Pelicans ( 10:30 ET, ESPN ). They can douse the internal and external fire by moving up the standings in the West and making a run for the postseason. They can do so with LeBron being \u201cactivated\u201d, dropping MVP-like performances and serving as an example to follow. Every team involved in the chase for one of the last few West playoff spots (Kings, Clippers, Spurs) have flaws. Yet none of them also have LeBron. Should the Lakers keep stumbling, then all eyes will be on LeBron and how he handles that. Will he play out a meaningless season, a distant experience for a player who\u2019s made the last eight NBA Finals? Or will he check out? Wherever LeBron and the Lakers go from here, drama will follow, and the biggest surprise is this isn\u2019t being caught on film and ready to be produced. Is it not entertaining enough? * * * Shaun Powell has covered the NBA for more than 25 years. You can e-mail him here , find his archive here and follow him on Twitter . Via a post on his Web site , the legendary Los Angeles Lakers and Milwaukee Bucks center said he will be selling his championship rings from 1980, \u201985, \u201987 and \u201988. All of those titles were earned while he was a member of the Lakers. In addition, he will be auctioning other items including game-worn uniforms and jerseys. One such item is the game-used and signed ball from his final game in the NBA in 1989. In his blog post, Abdul-Jabbar said he was auctioning with \u201cmuch of the proceeds\u201d going to benefit his Skyhook Foundation charity. That charity seeks to help kids learn about science, technology, engineering and math. \u201cMy sports memorabilia also have a history. My history. My life,\u201d Abdul-Jabbar said. \u201cAnd, oddly, since my life is still happening and ever-evolving, I am less personally attached to those items than I am to my desire to create new history for myself \u2014 and futures for others. Much of the proceeds from my auction will go to support my charity, the Skyhook Foundation, whose mission is to \u2018give kids a shot that can\u2019t be blocked.\u2019 \u201cSo, when it comes to choosing between storing a championship ring or trophy in a room, or providing kids with an opportunity to change their lives, the choice is pretty simple. Sell it all. Looking back on what I have done with my life, instead of gazing at the sparkle of jewels or gold plating celebrating something I did a long time ago, I\u2019d rather look into the delighted face of a child holding their first caterpillar and think about what I might be doing for their future. That\u2019s a history that has no price.\u201d The auction is being hosted by Goldin Auctions. Abdul-Jabbar also wrote that he is not having the auction because of financial problems. In addition to various items from his NBA playing days, Abdul-Jabbar is also auctioning off his class ring from Power Memorial High School, a pair of his iconic (game-worn) goggles, an ice bucket, a portrait of Abraham Lincoln, a VHS recording of his Hall of Fame induction in 1995 and various other awards from his past. Abdul-Jabbar, 71, is the NBA\u2019s all-time leading scorer with 38,387 points. After 32 consecutive games of scoring 30 or more points, though, that run came to an end in the Houston Rockets\u2019 119-111 home win against the Atlanta Hawks last night. Hall of Famer Wilt Chamberlain has the all-time mark for consecutive 30-point games at 65. During the streak, he scored 50 or more points four times, including a career-high 61 in a win at the Knicks on Jan. 23. And, already this season, he has joined Chamberlain, Michael Jordan and Rick Barry as the only players with 20 games of at least 40 points in the first 50 of a season. As we bid adieu to Harden\u2019s historic run, let\u2019s take a look back at some of his best performances from the 32-game streak \u2026 Every streak has to start somewhere and, sorry Lakers fans, but you were the first victim. Harden not only scored 50 points, but also added 10 rebounds, 11 assists and two steals for his second triple-double of the season. For good measure, Harden scored 11 points in the final five minutes to help seal a 126-111 win. His attempted step-back (step-back) wing jumper with with 54.6 seconds left over Ricky Rubio had the NBA Twitterverse up in arms . (The NBA later admitted it missed calling a travel on the move.) There\u2019s always an air of drama surrounding any Rockets-Thunder matchup from any number of storylines: the Harden vs. Russell Westbrook showdown, their past playoff matchups and their respective places in the Western Conference pecking order this season. Harden scored 41 on this night, marking his seventh straight game of 30 or more in the run. That was the most in the NBA since Westbrook had eight 30-point games back in November of 2016. The Thunder, Celtics, Pelicans and Grizzlies all suffered losses fueled by 40-point efforts from Harden from Christmas Day to New Year\u2019s Eve. As the calendar turned to 2019, Harden saved a strong dose of scoring venom for the rival Golden State Warriors. Madison Square Garden has been home to many great NBA moments and, on this date, several more took place . Harden scored a career-best 61 points, hitting the 30-point mark with three minutes to go in the first half. In this game, he became the first player with 60 points and 15 rebounds since 2000 (Shaquille O\u2019Neal), the first player to attempt 20 3-pointers and 20 free throws and the first player with three 55-point games in a month since 1963 (Chamberlain). Oh, and he also moved into fourth place on the 30-point game scoring streak. The Raptors and Rockets waged a classic that featured two Kia MVP types in Harden and Toronto\u2019s Kawhi Leonard. Fittingly, the game came down to a late 3-point attempt by Leonard, who was (of course) guarded by Harden. Leonard missed the shot and Harden notched his 22nd straight game with 30 or more points. In addition, he led his team and Houston\u2019s opponent in scoring for the 22nd straight game. That moved Harden past Jordan for the second-longest streak in NBA history behind Chamberlain, who did it in 40 in a row. He nailed it with 52.8 seconds to go, running his streak to 30 straight games, putting him on the cusp of the second-longest mark ever. No one can take the second-longest 30-point scoring run away from Harden. That was assured on this date when he notched 30 points, 10 rebounds and nine assists against the Lakers. However, it was unlikely to be a truly memorable night for Harden. Why? He fouled out with 1:24 remaining and his Rockets blew a 19-point lead to LeBron James and Co. in stunning fashion. Losing 50 of the 61 games your team plays \u2026 it\u2019s a deflating existence for any team. For the Phoenix Suns, this has summed up much of their season to date. For a veteran like Jamal Crawford, in his 19th NBA season, he knows it could be enough to break the collective spirit of an entire group. But Crawford also knows from experience what\u2019s on the other side of the Suns\u2019 current struggles. He\u2019s been around long enough, seen tough situations evolve often enough to know that there is nothing permanent in the NBA. There is always change coming, and you better be ready to adapt. You don\u2019t last as long as Crawford has in the NBA without understanding the NBA ecosystem and how quickly things can change. So, if the Suns are looking for some light at the end of this season\u2019s tumultuous journey, they need only pull up a seat next to their veteran sharpshooter and listen. Crawford shared some of his hard-earned wisdom with NBA.com\u2019s Sekou Smith as the Suns try to shake out of their funk tonight against the Miami Heat at American Airlines Arena: * * * Sekou Smith:  You\u2019ve been in this league a long time, 19 years. You could be ring chasing at this stage of your career. What are you doing here with the Suns? And what keeps you focused, and your juices flowing, on a team that\u2019s struggling the way the Suns are these days? Jamal Crawford:  Yeah, just the knowledge. Sometimes \u2026 and not just sometimes, it\u2019s really gratifying to see something go from point A to point C, rather than just being there for the end result. Sometimes the journey is greater than the destination. And for me, obviously, on the youngest team I\u2019ve been on in years, it\u2019s a challenge in some regards because you want guys to get it right away. And that\u2019s not always realistic. I know we want instant gratification in this league and in life. You see some guys get it, the light comes on, for some guys faster than others. And that\u2019s okay, everybody develops at his own pace. So you have to be patient and just fight through the tougher times and remember that the sweat equity always pays off. It\u2019s been a challenge, yes, but you have to make the best of every situation in this league if you are committed to being a true professional. SS:  Y ou\u2019ve been around this league for so long. You know how difficult it is to climb and how difficult it can be when you feel like you might be stuck in a tough situation. How does the vet keep the young guys locked in and focused without anything tangible (in terms of wins and losses) to cling to go? JC:  That\u2019s a really good question, because as I said, we are definitely an instant-gratification society. But there are moments you have to build on. So for that stretch of time it was like a lightbulb went off. \u2018These guys aren\u2019t just talking,\u2019 was the feedback. You are preaching the right things and the wins are coming to. That\u2019s when the magic happens. That was a big moment, but we didn\u2019t sustain it. SS:  Exactly, it only worked for a few games,. So how do you convince them that the hard work really pays off when they haven\u2019t really felt it? JC:  That\u2019s the challenge. When you get the wins and all of it comes together, you\u2019ve gotten through the hardest part. But when you get it going, the message hits home harder and that\u2019s when you take off as a group. But it has to be rooted in something guys can really see and feel. It can\u2019t just be words. We\u2019ve got plenty of that stuff going on, the hype, all over the league. Make sure it\u2019s real and then it\u2019s something you can really believe in. SS:  Devin Booker and DeAndre Ayton are clearly special talents. But how good can these guys be? You\u2019ve played with and against the best the game has to offer for nearly 20 years. What\u2019s the ceiling for these guys? JC:  Oh, these guys are stars. And they won\u2019t get that credit until we win. That\u2019s just the way the league is, always is and always will be. But you\u2019re talking about a 22-(Booker) and a 20-year-old (Ayton) and Book is already averaging 25 [points] and seven [assists] and [Ayton] is a guaranteed double-double. Book is already getting traps every game, getting double-teamed. He\u2019s already getting that kind of attention. But he\u2019s not going to get that respect until we win. Then he\u2019ll be an All-Star. Same with DeAndre. I\u2019m telling you.  SS:  So what\u2019s the toughest part of the transition for those guys? You\u2019ve been in this before, you\u2019ve lived it, trying to climb the food chain in this league. What\u2019s the toughest part of going from the young guy who can get numbers to a true impact player capable of changing outcomes and really leading a franchise? JC:  I think it\u2019s how you impact others and how that translates to winning. I mean, a guy can get 20 points a game. But if you are not winning, who\u2019s really paying attention? It\u2019s like, \u2018yeah, his game is nice. But I need to see him do it when it counts, when it really matters and something is on the line.\u2019 That\u2019s the flip side of when you see a guy who is just as good, but he\u2019s averaging 16 or 17 points on a team that\u2019s getting wins and respect. Everybody wants that, every guy who plays in this league is searching for that acknowledgement and ultimately that respect. Wining always cures all. And it\u2019s about timing. You have to be ready for it. SS:  You speak of timing, and I think about the way you play, the way you\u2019ve always played and cannot help but think you were a few years ahead of the time where you\u2019d have been an even more effective player given the wide-open style of this era. You\u2019ve played 19 years but it could have been crazy if that was 19 years in a different era, no? JC:  Oh my gosh, I\u2019m telling you. Totally different, totally different. And I say that because when I came into the league I was a point guard, if you took six [3-pointers] in a game you were going to be sitting on the bench, I don\u2019t care how good you were. I\u2019m serious. Back then it was about going to your dominant scorer, Shaq or Tim Duncan, or your dominant wing scorer, a Kobe [Bryant], T-Mac [Tracy McGrady], Paul Pierce or Allen Iverson, those guys. A point guard\u2019s job was to get them the ball. You weren\u2019t coming down the floor and shooting 30-footers off the dribble. A coach would be on you, and you could get that shot anytime. Work it around and get the ball where it\u2019s supposed to go. So yeah, the game has changed dramatically in my years in the league. I\u2019m sure it\u2019s fun for these [younger] guys, because it\u2019s definitely fun for me now [laughing]. SS:  Nineteen years, that\u2019s crazy. You look younger now than you did as a rookie. You\u2019ve got a full head of hair. You\u2019re always in game shape, I\u2019ve seen you in the middle of the summer and you look exactly the same. How many can you do? How long can you keep this up? JC:  Oh, I don\u2019t put a limit on it. I can keep going and going. And I will, as long as someone feels like I can bring something to the table, I\u2019ll be here. No limits. SS:  So how do you keep all of these guys on this team in that right mind while they are going through these struggles? You\u2019ve seen it, lived it, this kind of stuff can break a young team\u2019s collective spirit before they get to where a team like the Sacramento Kings are, when things start to turn in the right direction. JC:  You remind them that they have to be mindful of the bigger picture. It\u2019s like we\u2019re building a house. And right now we\u2019re on the foundation. And that\u2019s hard work. But there is beauty in the struggles. If you are learning lessons, it\u2019s not always just a loss you\u2019re taking. There\u2019s a lesson there, too. You have to be willing to accept that and not waver on your goals and your mission. I truly believe that.  SS:  I feel like you are uniquely positioned to spread the message. You\u2019ve played in so many different situations, big and small, winning and losing. There\u2019s some wisdom in your journey \u2014 that\u2019s clearly not over \u2014 that guys can learn from. You\u2019ve stayed true to the same mission you had from the start. Why did the struggle never turn you or lead you to sour on this process? JC:  Yes, yes. It wasn\u2019t my intention to keep my love of the game over everything. I love it so much. Basketball has given me everything. And even getting to this point. This might not be the ideal situation for anyone right now, but you know things can always get better. SS:  I should point out to you that you are playing the fewest amount of minutes [17.6 minutes per game] you\u2019ve played since your rookie season [17.2 mpg], taking the fewest amount of shot attempts since then [6 field goal attempts per game], playing a position (point guard) you haven\u2019t really played since the early days of your career \u2026 JC:  I know where you are going with this, and listen, I\u2019m in a great space \u2026 obviously I know I can still play at a high level, and can do much more then I am on the court. But this particular role at this time has turned into me trying to help others grow their game, and not about my own personal whatever \u2026 and there is a beauty in that as well. * * * Sekou Smith is a veteran NBA reporter and NBA TV analyst. But with an overall 18-game skid having been snapped on Thursday, the Knicks decided to address their home malaise next, earning a surprisingly comfortable 130-118 victory over the Spurs in which they led by as many as 23 and trailed for only a handful of possessions in the first quarter. It was such a momentous occasion that Samuel L. Jackson gave Knicks superfan Spike Lee a head\u2019s up at the Oscars. Brie Larson could scarcely believe it! The Knicks looked every bit like one of the league\u2019s worst teams in the opening moments as they gifted Spurs forward LaMarcus Aldridge with one of the easiest baskets he\u2019s ever \u201cscored.\u201d But if the Spurs expected the Knicks to keep presenting them with gifts, they were sorely mistaken. With New York already up eight late in the first half, recently-acquired Dennis Smith Jr. served notice that his team had come to play by coming mere inches from banishing Spurs forward Dennis Bertans to another dimension with what would have been a strong candidate for Dunk of the Year. It was a challenge the Spurs were unable to answer as New York led by at least eight throughout the second half. Damyean Dotson led the way with 27 points and eight 3-pointers, and Smith, Kevin Knox and Mitchell Robinson all posted double-doubles. Smith\u2019s included 13 assists, including this beauty to Robinson that punctuated the Knicks\u2019 first home win since Dec. 1: \u201cOur guys needed to feel that at home,\u201d Knicks coach David Fizdale said. \u201cThe fans were amazing, and we got a lot of contributions. We still made a couple of mistakes \u2026 but I\u2019m really proud of how hard they competed.\u201d In addition to the Spurs losing for the sixth time in seven outings, the LA Clippers suffered a 123-96 beating by the Denver Nuggets as the race for the final playoffs spots in the Western Conference got even tighter. How tight, you ask? Just three games separate the fifth-place Houston Rockets and the Sacramento Kings in ninth, with the Utah Jazz, Spurs and Clippers sandwiched between them. The Nuggets, meanwhile, continued to keep the heat on the Golden State Warriors, whose lead atop the West was sliced to a single game with two more meetings remaining on March 8 and April 2.  Over in the East, the first-place Milwaukee Bucks got a huge assist from the Orlando Magic, who took advantage of Kawhi Leonard\u2019s rest day to rout the Toronto Raptors 113-98 . While the Bucks lead the Raptors by only two games, their position is much stronger than it looks. In addition to having an additional game advantage in the loss column, they also hold the head-to-head tie-breaker. As if all that wasn\u2019t enough, they\u2019ve also got the league\u2019s fourth-easiest schedule over their remaining 23 games. There are worse ways to celebrate wins. Backtracking to Saturday\u2019s 12-game slate, check out this tidbit: Little wonder the NBA is in the midst of its highest-scoring season, with a collective scoring average of 110.9 points per team per game, since 1970-71."},{"id":35361,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/ralph-lawler-la-clippers-broadcast-legacy","date":"2019-02-24","title":"Oh me, oh my! As retirement nears, Ralph Lawler reflects on life calling Clippers games","content":" LOS ANGELES \u2014 Lord knows this franchise has racked up enough \u201cLs\u201d in the past and sadly, the LA Clippers are bracing for a few more at season\u2019s end. Loyalty, longevity, loquaciousness, they\u2019re about to lose all that. All because the man who graced the team with those qualities has tweaked his own definition of Lawler\u2019s Law: the first Clippers broadcaster to reach 40 years on the job must retire. This is it for Ralph Lawler, the enduring voice of the franchise, the perky purveyor of Clippers basketball. He\u2019s the talking head who married \u201coh me!\u201d with \u201coh my!\u201d to create a catch-phrase that squealed how the Clippers did something special on the court at that very moment. \u201cI\u2019d rather quit a year too early than a year too late,\u201d explained Lawler, 80, whose standards always ran high while doing radio and then TV play-by-play for the Clippers. It is appropriate and respectful to lavish a parting gift on those who walk into the sunset. For Lawler, who has watched over 2,000 Clippers losses, there\u2019s an urge to give him Visine. Or better, a place in the media wing of the Naismith Memorial Basketball Hall of Fame, which happened last weekend. Because nobody in basketball history did more with less. How about this trick? Try keeping listeners locked into games that end badly, as it was for vast stretches of Lawler\u2019s time with the Clippers. Lawler always had the respect of his broadcasting peers but none of their good fortune while calling Clippers games. The team has never reached a conference finals and the contrast has been especially stark here in LA, which was roamed by broadcasting legends like Chick Hearn and Vin Scully. It\u2019s the broadcaster\u2019s job to bring events and people to life while blowing excitement through the mic and into everyone\u2019s ears. Hearn narrated \u201cShowtime\u201d and the Kobe Bryant-Shaquille O\u2019Neal teams . Scully described Kirk Gibson\u2019s World Series homer in 1988 . Lawler explained Benoit Benjamin . Who had the tougher job? He weathered a franchise relocation, the working conditions in the dumpy LA Sports Arena, a string of crummy injuries to Danny Manning \u2026 and Ron Harper \u2026 and Shaun Livingston. There was the failed promise of Michael Olowokandi and, of course, the weird rise and shameful fall of owner Donald T. Sterling . Yet, as the Clippers\u2019 seasons ran aimlessly into each other, Lawler survived and thrived. As team broadcasters tend to become part of the family to their audiences as they age, Lawler transformed from your older brother to uncle to father to grandfather to great grandfather. And undertaker, to those in the audience he outlived. In fact, he\u2019s only missed three games in his 40 years on the job.  His punch-lines and signature calls endeared him to fans, and up until the franchise began winning more regularly a decade ago, were pretty much the best thing going for the Clippers. \u201cLawler\u2019s Law\u201d meant the first team to 100 points wins the game. The \u201coh me, oh my\u201d reaction was pure excitement. Lawler would warn fans to \u201cfasten your seatbelts\u201d to prepare for a tight finish and shouted \u201cbingo!\u201d each time a former Clipper named Bobby \u201cBingo\u201d Smith scored a hoop. When Bingo left, \u201cbingo!\u201d stayed. And, Lawler is the only NBA broadcaster who speaks into a hand-held microphone \u2014 because he finds it easier. From 1978-79, his first season, through 2010-11, the Clippers only had three winning seasons, but don\u2019t reach for a hanky on Lawler\u2019s behalf. He\u2019s had the best seat in the house and let the record show he never lost a game. \u201cI realized early on, back in the early \u201880s that I have no control over winning and losing, so why should I get too invested in winning and losing?\u201d he said. \u201cI invest 100 percent of my energy into the broadcast. We\u2019d lose a ballgame and I\u2019m going, `Man, we had a good show.\u2019 \u201cLook, I wish they\u2019d won 10 championships. I wish they were the Boston Celtics. But I love the craft. I love to broadcast, the challenge of bringing a bad game to life and making it entertaining and informative. I have loved every single second. There was a year we won 12 and lost 70 and I loved every one of those 82 games.\u201d Besides, Lawler\u2019s been with champions. He began his career in Philadelphia with the NHL\u2019s Flyers and his timing was better than Rolex, because the city celebrated two Stanley Cups . He didn\u2019t know a red line from a blue line, and it didn\u2019t matter, because he could articulate a brawl and the \u201cBroad Street Bullies\u201d had plenty of those. \u201cThe gloves are off and there they go!\u201d Lawler would scream; the audience ate it up. He left for San Diego for the great weather and an NBA team that moved from Buffalo and renamed the Clippers, and a legacy began. It was actually interrupted twice, when management tried to replace him for no reason other than to go with someone different. The first time was in 1982 when he was doing Clippers radio and the station changed owners. As the season began, Lawler worked in real estate and, one day, he and his future wife Jo went for a walk on the beach near a house he had listed. \u201cHere comes Donald Sterling walking toward us,\u201d Lawler recalled. \u201cI turned to Jo and was like, \u2018My God, do we want to have this exchange?\u2019 So we walked up and made small talk. I said, \u2018Hey, we got a house with a jacuzzi, might as well jump in and have some wine.\u2019 He said yeah. \u201cAt one point he said, \u2018Why don\u2019t you work for me anymore?\u2019 I said \u2018because you didn\u2019t hire me.\u2019 He said, \u2018we gotta change that.\u2019 Next day I got a call from the general manager saying we need you back. Were it not for that walk on the beach I\u2019m quite sure I would not be here today.\u201d When the Clippers moved to L.A. in 1984, then-GM Carl Scheer wanted a flashier presence on the mic and broke the bad news to Lawler. So back to real estate he went, and a guy named Eddie Ducette took over, and two weeks into the season, Lawler\u2019s phone rang. It was Scheer, sounding desperate. \u201cWe made a big mistake,\u201d he said. Officially, then, Lawler has missed only three games. One because of LA traffic \u2014 Lawler at the time was still commuting from his home in La Quinta, between LA and San Diego. The mother of all jams happened and it took him six hours to go six miles. Stuck on the 405, he turned around at halftime. The second time, he needed surgery to remove kidney stones. He scheduled the procedure in the morning so he\u2019d make the game that night \u2026 but a tube stuck down his throat stole his voice temporarily. The third time, he and broadcast partner Michael Smith were suspended for one game in 2009 for comments made about the homeland of Memphis Grizzlies center Hamed Haddadi. That one burns Lawler to this day. \u201cI pronounced Iran wrong,\u201d he said. \u201cIt was 100 percent unwarranted. I did absolutely nothing wrong. One person wrote an email saying he was offended, and this was the same guy who came down and asked for an autograph and photo when the suspension was over.\u201d It was the first time anyone in the organization can recall the normally mild-mannered Lawler turn angry, but not the last. He was deeply hurt by the behavior of Sterling and the release of tapes where the former owner was overheard making racially-insensitive remarks about black players on his team as well as about NBA legend Magic Johnson. All of that, and more , led to Sterling being banned for life by the NBA and, eventually, his trust selling the team in 2014 for $2 billion. The team gave Lawler a prepared message to read over the air before the next game, and while his stomach still churned, he never mangled a single syllable of that statement. \u201cI felt sick,\u201d he said. \u201cWhat he did embarrassed me. It hurt that I had represented this man for the previous 30 years. That\u2019s a weekend that will live in infamy for me and the franchise.\u201d Not that Lawler didn\u2019t see this coming. There was a time when he and Sterling were on solid terms, especially during the early years in San Diego, when \u201cI was Ralph to him and he was Donald to me.\u201d But soon: \u201cIt was Mr. Sterling to me, or DTS. He liked to be called by his initials, all of a sudden.\u201d Not long ago, Sterling attended a coach\u2019s meeting in training camp and Dave Wohl, an assistant coach at the time, turned to the owner and said: \u201cDon, this is what we have to do \u2026 \u201c Sterling quickly corrected him: \u201c Mr. Sterling , please.\u201d Lawler does say this much: \u201cIf that hadn\u2019t happened and Sterling wasn\u2019t removed, Steve wouldn\u2019t be the owner today and that would be unfortunate.\u201d That\u2019s Steve as in Ballmer, the software billionaire who took control of the club three years ago and essentially opened the windows in the building and let the stench out. Lawler said: \u201cHe\u2019s exciting and encouraging. He\u2019s \u2018Call me Steve.\u2019 Last year we\u2019re walking into the tunnel and going through security screening, and a security woman, who\u2019s been there for years, she walks up and says, \u2018Hey Steve, how ya doing?\u2019 That\u2019s who he is. \u201cHe had a big meeting with the entire staff and handed out his email address to everybody. If you have any problems, he said to let him know, he\u2019ll get to it. Look, he\u2019s demanding and a tough taskmaster. He\u2019s not going to be patient for long periods of time but he is everything the coach and GM want in an owner.\u201d Lawler gets emotional about two others, one a former member of the organization, one current. Bill Walton suffered through a series of foot surgeries which prevented him from becoming the franchise savior when the team began in San Diego. He partnered with Lawler on team broadcasts in the 1990s and their friendship deepened. They vacationed for 18 days in the Grand Canyon, rafting the Colorado River. Their conversations always ran thick, and with Walton, how could it not? \u201cWorking with Walton on TV changed me, made me better,\u201d said Lawler. \u201cThat was a graduate course in having fun. It really helped me turn the corner in terms of how I approach the job.\u201d Also, Lawler was diagnosed with prostate cancer 10 years ago and within moments of returning home, there was a knock at the door. \u201cBill and his wife,\u201d said Lawler. \u201cAnd then he came back the following week and took us out to dinner. The nicest, most generous human I\u2019ve ever met outside of my dad.\u201d  The other difference-maker for Lawler is coach Doc Rivers. Lawler was ready to quit the business 10 years ago, but then Rivers arrived and the culture changed. The \u201cLob City\u201d era reinvigorated Lawler and the Clippers\u2019 fan base. The club suddenly made a habit of making the playoffs. And seat belts were being fastened on the couches of Clippers fans watching at home. Suddenly, winning mattered to Lawler, after all. \u201cThis was the kind of stuff you dreamed of having, after all those dark years,\u201d he said. \u201cThey have made it tough to leave. So this is a very emotional closing act for me. It will be almost impossible for me to replace this.\u201d And so on his final game this season, right after the buzzer, the only NBA broadcaster who holds a hot mic will let it drop after 40 years, and when it hits the floor, it can only make one sound: bingo! * * * Shaun Powell has covered the NBA for more than 25 years. Targeting 2024 for new digs, Ballmer and the organization believe exiting Staples Center, where they share space with their city rival Los Angeles Lakers, is the prudent move for the future. \u201c[We] need our own house,\u201d Ballmer insists. Yet the Clippers\u2019 proposed arena in Inglewood, where The Forum remains a concert and event venue, has legal obstacles to clear before the project can advance to the next stage. \u201cWe\u2019re going through the permitting process,\u201d Ballmer told NBA.com Thursday in a wide-ranging interview. \u201cAnd an environmental process, and we\u2019re going through that right now. We have some folks pushing back on us, primarily Madison Square Garden and the Knicks, if you will. They own The Forum, which is a concert venue, and they don\u2019t want to see a new concert venue, which any new basketball arena would be. So we\u2019re getting some pushback. \u201cBut 2024 is our target. And we\u2019ve given ourselves some time to get ready. And 2024 comes faster than you think, so we\u2019re pushing along down the path. We\u2019re excited. We\u2019ve seen some preliminary exterior designs \u2026 can\u2019t show them to you yet. But the community will see them not too long from now.\u201d Ballmer\u2019s vision for the new building is for it to be crafted with basketball experience as the primary focus. There have been scant public details about the project, which would be built on 23 acres of mostly vacant land. The site would include not only an 18,000-to 20,000 seat arena, but also a practice facility, team offices, sports medicine clinic, parking facilities and more. \u201cIt\u2019s about the ability to get it right,\u201d said Ballmer, the billionaire and former Microsoft CEO who bought the Clippers in 2014. \u201cWe\u2019re not putting hockey in the building. I don\u2019t think most people know just how big a difference it can make to not have hockey. You get everybody closer to the floor. The sightlines are a lot better. We\u2019re talking about how much leg room to give people, how much width. I like energy. I want people pumping and thumping in the seats. But you\u2019ve still got to have some bars and clubs. \u201cWe\u2019re trying to pull you back in. Some buildings, in my opinion, try and push you out a little bit to the bars and clubs. Then it\u2019s more of a different kind of social experience. We\u2019re trying to support both. But we want people who really love the game in the building.\u201d The new arena would provide the Clippers with an identity they simply have not had, something that sharing space with the Lakers and their 16 championship banners has always overshadowed. Ballmer took over a team that had stars on the roster \u2014 Chris Paul, Blake Griffin and DeAndre Jordan \u2014 and in the coaching and front office ranks with Doc Rivers. They were winning and going to the Western Conference playoffs while the Lakers were on the downside of the Kobe Bryant era and missing from the postseason picture. And yet the Clippers still had to battle history and image problems in a city dominated for generations by the Lakers and their prevalent fan culture, one that is pervasive in the Southland and beyond.  \u201cI think we made some progress since Blake, DeAndre and Chris,\u201d Ballmer said of the team\u2019s former stars, each of whom has moved on in trades or free agency. \u201cWe had a winning team basically since these guys came to the Clippers. We changed the guys, but we\u2019ve never been the big dog in town. Now there\u2019s only one other town in America where you have two NBA teams and that\u2019s in New York. So for me, it was a whole other experience in Los Angeles.\u201d Ballmer lives in Seattle, but discovered his love for the game as an 11-year-old in suburban Detroit, watching the Pistons and witnessing the appreciation the hometown team and its stars were afforded from local fans. \u201cFor me growing up in Detroit, it\u2019s the Pistons. It\u2019s always the Pistons,\u201d Ballmer said. \u201cBut in L.A., you have to think about it differently. Not only do we play in the same building, we don\u2019t have the championship pedigree. So you know what, we need our own house. We\u2019re going to define our own identity, in our own house. \u201cWe\u2019d like to build a team that\u2019s tough, competitive, hard-playing guys. I\u2019m not saying every team doesn\u2019t have some aspect of that. But I want that to be our tone \u2026 tough, competitive, gritty and resilient. And I think you have to give people their own house to go and do it. We\u2019re doing it all, the practice facility and everything. And in 2024, we\u2019ll be the newest stadium out there.\u201d That doesn\u2019t mean Ballmer is waiting on 2024 to field a competitive team. The Clippers are 32-27 in possession of the eighth and final playoff spot with 23 games left and Ballmer says, charging ahead with plans to hold on to that postseason berth at all costs. Even after trading Tobias Harris to Philadelphia in a six-player deal at the trade deadline, a deal that netted the Clippers assets including rookie guard Landry Shamet, the Sixers\u2019 own 2020 protected first-round Draft pick and an unprotected 2021 first-round pick from the Miami Heat, Ballmer said the goal remains the same this season. Ballmer loves the roster the Clippers have now and loves the process of continuing to build the basketball side as much as he enjoys being immersed in the business side. \u201cCan I use an analogy? And I don\u2019t want to take it too far,\u201d Ballmer said. \u201cPutting together the roster is a little bit like product development in any other business. Yeah, you\u2019re going to sell and you\u2019re going to market it. But how do you get that right product, the beautiful product the Microsoft Surface or the Xbox or even to competitors to Microsoft, the iPhone. You really want to \u2026 and it\u2019s not easy. You\u2019ve really got to think it through. All of the details matter. \u201cIt\u2019s fun. It\u2019s a little tricky. The other thing, I guess I sort of knew, it\u2019s not like you have invite flexibility. People like to say, \u2018Just go build your roster.\u2019 But it\u2019s really kind of clever. You have to figure all of this out. How does the Draft work? How does free agency work? How does the trade process work? Free agents. Drafts. Trades. How can you use the tools? It\u2019s not like you can trade for anybody in the league. But before you get involved [as an owner], it\u2019s like \u2018Trade for anybody, hire whoever you want, sign whatever free agent you want. I\u2019m always going to get a good draft pick.\u2019 And that\u2019s just not the way it works.\u201d Having fewer degrees of freedom forces you to be even more insightful, Ballmer said. It\u2019s also what keeps his kinetic energy on full blast. \u201cI loved it before, I love it now and we\u2019re probably a little more flexible now,\u201d Ballmer said, \u201cbut we\u2019re in it now. We\u2019re competing for the playoffs because that\u2019s who we are. We\u2019re never going to not compete. I know some other teams have taken some steps back. We bought ourselves a little more flexibility. I\u2019m glad to see our guys doing well now that they\u2019ve moved on. But I love the guys on our team. The league has sent a proposal to the National Basketball Players Association on lowering the minimum age for entering the NBA Draft from 19 to 18, and the union discussed the contents at a meeting in the Bahamas earlier this week, a person with knowledge of the matter told The Associated Press on Thursday. The person spoke to the AP on condition of anonymity because neither side released the proposal publicly. USA Today Sports first reported the proposal being sent. The proposal changed hands during NBA All-Star Weekend and was not in reaction to Duke star Zion Williamson, quite possibly the No. 1 pick in this year\u2019s draft, suffering a Grade 1, or minor, sprain of his right knee on Wednesday night. Williamson, a freshman, is widely expected to be in the NBA next season and forgo his final three seasons of collegiate eligibility. Neither the league nor the players\u2019 union has hidden the fact that both sides want the current system changed. NBA Commissioner Adam Silver said last July that it was time to revert back to the policy that will allow players to go into the league right out of high school, something that will have to be collectively bargained with the players. The NBPA has had previous talks with the NBA on the idea, which is likely to be in place by the 2022 draft. \u201cI think it\u2019s a good idea,\u201d Boston\u2019s Jayson Tatum, who went to the NBA after one season at Duke, said at All-Star weekend. \u201cIf you\u2019re good enough to come out of high school, I feel like you should be able to. But I don\u2019t make those decisions.\u201d Golden State\u2019s DeMarcus Cousins, who played at Kentucky, told reporters Thursday that knowing what he knows now makes him question why players need to play college basketball \u2013 especially if they\u2019re NBA-ready. \u201cI don\u2019t understand the point of it,\u201d Cousins said of the `one-and-done\u2019 rule. \u201cWhat\u2019s the difference between 18 and 19 and 17 and 18? You\u2019re immature, you\u2019re young, you\u2019re ignorant to life in general. So what\u2019s really the difference? You\u2019ve still got a lot of growing to do as a man.\u201d The one-and-done rule has been in place since the 2006 draft.
