If this happens, this would be the one of the most embarrassing events of LeBron James\u2019 otherwise dreamy career. That\u2019s all. Nothing else at stake here. Yes, the Los Angeles Lakers missing the playoffs would almost guarantee Luke Walton will not return as coach next season. The team\u2019s braintrust, led by team president Magic Johnson, would feel plenty of pinch to upgrade the club this summer. But those are down-the-road worries and repercussions. At the center of it all is the pride of the game\u2019s greatest player and a potential rewind to the 2004-05 season \u2014 the last time James missed the playoffs. Back then, James had a good excuse: he was only in his second season, expectations were low and his team (the Cleveland Cavaliers) wasn\u2019t exactly dripping talent. This is different. This is the first year of LeBron joining a historic franchise and the white-hot glow that comes with that. And this is the NBA so accustomed to, and somewhat reliant on, LeBron playing in springtime. Don\u2019t forget, LeBron\u2019s teams have made eight straight trips to The Finals . He said twice Wednesday how he will be \u201cdifferent\u201d in the remaining two months of the season, dropping hints that \u201cplayoff LeBron\u201d will debut here in mid-February out of necessity. \u201cI haven\u2019t been in this position in a while,\u201d he said, meaning one game under .500 after the All-Star break. \u201cThis is where we are right now. I\u2019m going to be a little bit different, a little earlier than I\u2019d like to be. My level of intensity has to be a little bit different.\u201d The Push For The Playoffs has become the Lakers\u2019 new and unexpected slogan that will text everyone involved. It won\u2019t be simple or easy, even if LeBron plays full blast. The schedule is treacherous, with the Lakers sporting the West\u2019s fourth-toughest remaining schedule . The Lakers are 28-29, three games out of the No. 8 spot with 25 to play (13 of which are road games). They must play, among others, the two conference leaders (Golden State and Milwaukee Bucks), as well as the Toronto Raptors, Houston Rockets, Boston Celtics, Denver Nuggets, Portland Trail Blazers, Utah Jazz (twice) and Oklahoma City Thunder. Last season, it took 47 wins to clinch the No. 8 spot . Assuming that\u2019s the mark again, the Lakers must finish 19-6. Understand, the Lakers haven\u2019t won four straight games, their longest winning streak of the season, since mid-December. And even if they reach the playoffs, it\u2019ll likely mean a first-round date with the two-time defending-champion Warriors. \u201cStranger things have happened, but it would be weird to have the playoffs and not have him in the playoffs,\u201d said Warriors guard Klay Thompson. \u201cLike, weird.\u201d The LA Clippers, currently the No. 8 seed, have dwindling motivation and ability to make the playoffs. They traded their best player (Tobias Harris) earlier this month to create cap room for a summer free-agent run. If they make the playoffs, their No. 1 pick goes to the Celtics. If they fall into the lottery, they keep it. More realistically, this is about the Lakers competing down the stretch against the energized and hungry Sacramento Kings. They haven\u2019t made the playoffs in 13 seasons and don\u2019t have a No. 1 pick in the 2019 draft. The Lakers are also fighting the proud San Antonio Spurs, who haven\u2019t missed the playoffs since coach Gregg Popovich\u2019s first season. Following their Christmas Day win in Oakland, the Lakers were No. 4 in the West . But the season was thrown for a loop with LeBron\u2019s groin injury-induced absence and other Lakers injuries and suspensions. The Lakers still aren\u2019t at full strength until Lonzo Ball recovers from his ankle sprain . That should come soon, although he has yet to practice. LeBron has made a habit of carrying lesser teams to the playoffs and beyond , although he did that in the East without missing many games. This is another, different hill to climb. \u201cI\u2019m looking forward to the second half of the season, looking forward to seeing what we can do to get back into this playoff race,\u201d James said after the All-Star Game. \u201cThat\u2019s my mindset. LeBron defied age once again and put up Kia MVP-like numbers, including a reliable touch on 3-pointers . JaVale McGee was a pleasantly surprising source of offense, Rajon Rondo was efficiently steady and the young core of Ball, Brandon Ingram and Kyle Kuzma had their moments. At the All-Star break, LeBron and Rondo had just returned, Ball was hurt, McGee was the No. 2 center ( behind the now-departed Ivica Zubac ), Ingram was an enigma and Kuzma was rising as a solid No. 2 scorer. And of course, the Davis drama weighed on the locker room. \u201cAll I know,\u201d Kuzma said, \u201cis when we were healthy, we won. We were fine. The goal is to get back to that. Let\u2019s get a healthy team and then we\u2019ll see. I\u2019m confident in what we can do.\u201d This was always designated as an exploratory season for the Lakers with LeBron. Entering the season, they had young players without playoff experience. They had veterans on one-year contracts serving as bridge-gap players so the Lakers can keep their salary cap flexible for 2019. In a sense, there was never any false hopes by management of making the Warriors sweat. But making the playoffs? That was expected. > The West:  Who can contend with Warriors? \u201cIt was our goal at the beginning of the season and still our goal,\u201d LeBron said. If they do, the Lakers might make it interesting in the first round if they see, for example, the inexperienced Denver Nuggets (or any other non-Warriors team). If they don\u2019t, then it\u2019s an embarrassment for the Lakers and setback for LeBron. One of those rest disadvantage games is at the end of a 5-games-in-7 days stretch from March 2-8 that includes road games against the Spurs, Blazers and Clippers. Rest advantage \/ Rest disadvantage: Games in which one team (at a disadvantage) played the day before and the other (at an advantage) did not. This season, teams are 129-85 (.603) with a rest advantage, 97-42 (.698) at home and 32-43 (.427) on the road. There will be no easy matchups in the Western Conference playoffs, but there will be an advantage to finishing second or third. If the Thunder can do that after playing the league\u2019s toughest post-break schedule, they will have earned it. It wasn\u2019t supposed to be pretty this season over on this side of the NBA. With LeBron James\u2019 decision to spend his late prime in Los Angeles , the Eastern Conference looked initially like a default situation. Somebody was going to win it, whether they were worthy of challenging whoever came out of the West (subliminal: Golden State!) or not. > The West:  Who can contend with Warriors? Nine days later, though, Toronto traded for the San Antonio Spurs\u2019 unhappy star, Kawhi Leonard . The Milwaukee bucks perked up instantly under the tutelage of new coach Mike Budenholzer . The Philadelphia 76ers flipped Dario Saric and Robert Covington for Minnesota\u2019s All-Star disruptor Jimmy Butler . And lo and behold, the East began to look not merely interesting but formidable. So much so that an arms race ensued at the trade deadline . The Raptors (Marc Gasol), the Sixers (Tobias Harris) and the Bucks (Nikola Mirotic) all upgraded their talent bases. Boston? Well, the Celtics kept their powder dry presumably for the Anthony Davis sweepstakes this summer . But then, with Kyrie Irving around after having missed last spring\u2019s playoffs and Gordon Hayward back, period, it could be argued those guys already got their infusion of help. And at a level higher than any of their rivals. Then there\u2019s the plucky Indiana Pacers, who seem almost to have been galvanized by the loss of their star player, Victor Oladipo . With insights from a few NBA advance scouts (who remain anonymous here), here is a breakdown of the East\u2019s Fab Five, in order of their position in the standings as the dash to the postseason begins. * * * Other than the Lakers (James) and the Rockets (James Harden), no team in the NBA \u2014 and certainly no team in the East \u2014 is more dependent on one player than the Bucks. Giannis Antetokounmpo probably is the leading candidate for 2019 Kia Most Valuable Player at this point, but the talent and impact gap between him and Milwaukee\u2019s second-best player is greater than any of these other contenders. The Bucks are 13.7 points better than their opponents when \u201cThe Greek Freak\u201d is on the floor. They\u2019re 2-2 in games he has missed vs. 41-12 when he plays. Now imagine even a minor injury that costs him, say, two games in a best-of-seven series. Yeah, trouble. Still, if Antetokounmpo stays healthy and gets rest late in games when wins are secure, Milwaukee has a legit shot at its first Finals trip since 1974 . The ensemble cast around Antetokounmpo fits him perfectly, spreading the floor to open penetration lanes and seizing on the kick-outs when defenders converge on him. The Bucks are third in 3-pointers made , second in attempts and \u2014 if you take out Antetokounmpo\u2019s 29-of-130 \u2014 they rise from 34.9 percent to 35.7 percent in 3-point accuracy. And this is without Mirotic. Defensively the Bucks are taking away the other guys\u2019 3-point opportunities, sweeping the defensive boards and relying on Antetokounmpo\u2019s and Brook Lopez\u2019s size as needed in the paint. There\u2019s a noticeable bump in Bucks chemistry this season that those inside the locker room will tell you sparks winning, rather than vice versa. Two ongoing goals have kept them focused and resilient, too: Milwaukee has yet to lose two games in a row, and the Bucks have struck back hard whenever facing a team that beat them previously. None of the East powers stood to benefit more from James\u2019 shift from Eastern to Pacific time zones than these guys. It wasn\u2019t just his basketball excellence that had gotten in the Raptors\u2019 way postseason after postseason \u2014 it was his dominance in the East ( eight consecutive Finals trips ) that had tormented them. Not since, oh, Michael Jordan vs. the New York Knicks had a single superstar seemed to pitch a tent inside an opponent\u2019s heads. Even a status quo version of Toronto, led by Kyle Lowry and DeMar DeRozan, might have seen different results this time. But with Leonard, Gasol and underrated buyout pickup Jeremy Lin, this is a bolder, mentally freed squad that could be more efficient than last spring\u2019s edition. Gasol figures to keep divvying minutes with Serge Ibaka. But as well as Toronto played with Jonas Valanciunas, Gasol should be that and more. Similar size, more adept as a passer and shooter. \u201cHe\u2019s so skilled and he\u2019s really motivated,\u201d a scout said of Gasol and this opportunity to salvage a difficult season. \u201cAnd they got out of a couple contracts in C.J. Miles and Valanciunas.\u201d Granted, Toronto has gone 13-3 when Leonard has not played. But keeping one of the NBA\u2019s elite two-way players healthy is a must once the playoffs start. Forward Pascal Siakam might be the favorite at this point for the Kia Most Improved Player Award (16.1 ppg, 7.0 rpg and 55 percent shooting). Lin stabilizes the backcourt, especially while Fred Van Vleet recovers from thumb surgery . It was not without some downside risk that boss Masai Ujiri changed coaches, firing Dwane Casey to promote assistant Nick Nurse . But Nurse has tweaked the Raptors masterfully. They won their last six games before the break and 10 of 13. Not only are they 24-5 at home (and 16-6 against the West), but they are 9-4 in games decided by three points or fewer. As our John Schuhmann points out : Toronto has the easiest schedule in the league from here till the postseason (only two back-to-backs, with 16 of 23 games against foes .500 or worse). The Pacers exit the All-Star break third in the East , one game ahead of both Philadelphia and Boston in the standings. Most insiders and even Indiana fans figure them to dip to fifth, considering the loss of Oladipo. Still, it speaks volumes about the roster and staff that they\u2019re projected not just to hang onto a playoff berth, but keep a gap between themselves and the last three seeds. Granted, being up 8 1\/2 games on sixth-place Brooklyn with 24 left to play is swell math regardless. But the Pacers are the closest thing the East has to Monty Python\u2019s \u201cHoly Grail\u201d Black Knight , the feisty sentry who refuses to quit regardless of how many limbs he loses. It might not say much for Oladipo in a classic, how-much-do-they-miss-him MVP argument that Indiana looked locked into a third-, fourth- or fifth-place finish with or without him. But it says plenty about the Pacers\u2019 fortitude. \u201cI think they\u2019re going to stay in the battle,\u201d one scout said. \u201cThey\u2019re very well-coached. They\u2019ve got a lot of good character guys. And Wes Matthews isn\u2019t Victor Oladipo, but he will help them. They\u2019re a team .\u201d Indiana has tough, no-muss-or-fuss performers such as Thaddeus Young and Domantas Sabonis. Coach Nate McMillan and his staff are underrated on an annual basis. And this team rises and falls on its defense ( first in fewest points allowed and second in defensive rating ). That\u2019s key, because the Pacers don\u2019t have the firepower of the East\u2019s presumed Big Four, and the offense has been more raggedy without Oladipo. \u201cYou know what they say, \u2018defense travels,\u2019 too,\u201d said the scout. The Pacers are 8.5 points worse defensively away from home, but they have managed a 16-12 road mark. That\u2019s the East\u2019s third-best mark behind the Bucks (20-9) and the Raptors (19-11). As soon as Harris joined the Sixers , the quickie description of this team became: Best starting lineup in the NBA other than Golden State. They have All-Stars, real or worthy, at all five spots, making it impossible to double Joel Embiid, Ben Simmons or any of them, frankly. \u201cI\u2019d worry about their depth,\u201d a scout said. \u201cThen with Jimmy Butler, he just doesn\u2019t quite fit their team, for me. Yes, he can defend, but he\u2019s not a space-the-court jump shooter and he needs the ball a lot for their offense.\u201d With all the frontcourt depth Philadelphia has, you can mix and match as needed. Coach Brett Brown should never have to rely entirely on reserves unless he wants to (or it\u2019s garbage time). Butler is quite happy to take charge of second-unit duties for the ball dominance it offers. Another trade deadline move that could help came in sending Markelle Fultz to Orlando for Jonathon Simmons and a first-round pick . The pick makes up a bit for the one they shipped to Boston in a pick swap before the 2017 draft . It also closes the book on Fultz and what looks like a regrettable detour in \u201cThe Process,\u201d up there with Nerlens Noel and Jahlil Okafor. Additionally, new GM Elton Brand has been impressive in his early days on the job, so the buyout market still is in play. The \u201cfragile\u201d days of Embiid sure appear to be over \u2026 or did, until Wednesday\u2019s reveal of left knee soreness. And few other teams run as \u201chot\u201d as the Sixers emotionally, which can be a positive if directed toward the Finals prize. It would seem to be a terrific problem to have: too many quality players. Yet Boston has sagged this season in part because of a blurry pecking order, an abundance of talent in which no two or three talented leaders have emerged to embody the will of coach Brad Stevens on the group. There are personalities and insecurities involved in that, such that even a presumptive conference favorite can get sidetracked. Said one scout: \u201cWhen a team gets deeper and a guy\u2019s minutes get pinched, sometimes when they do get out there, they press.\u201d Let\u2019s not overlook the Davis speculation, either. Boston has been all about the summer on that, so the uncertainty hasn\u2019t been as pressing as for the Lakers. Still, there are young Celtics players who wonder how long they\u2019ll be around. Then there\u2019s the challenge of being the East\u2019s hunted, at least when this began. \u201cExpectations were so high for that team,\u201d said another scout, \u201cand some of them may have thought it would be easier than it\u2019s been. Working Hayward back into the rotation was a bigger challenge than many expected. There are young guys who are playing for contracts a little bit.\u201d Hayward has been better lately, averaging 14.6 points and 4.0 assists in February vs. 10.4 ppg and 3.8 rpg in December . Irving reigns as the best finisher in the league and more playoff battle-hardened than any other player in the conference. And yet the Celtics have gone 9-2 when he hasn\u2019t played. That might say less about him than it does the rest of the roster. When a herd like this gets thinned, a more streamlined pecking order can emerge. Besides, Terry Rozier is a defensive upgrade on Irving. The Celtics have confidence built over the past two seasons against the Sixers and they seem up to any challenge posed by the Raptors. The Bucks, however, could pose a matchup because Boston\u2019s frontline that gives up a few too many inches to Milwaukee\u2019s when Al Horford plays. * * * Steve Aschburner has written about the NBA since 1980. As such, hardly anybody knew initially about the demand. If anyone understands what Anthony Davis is thinking, asking for a trade out of New Orleans with nearly 1 1\/2 seasons left on his contract, it\u2019s Abdul-Jabbar. His trade request came with two years left on his contract in Milwaukee. Eventually, he got his wish in the summer that followed his ask and got traded to the Los Angeles Lakers . \u201cI think that the players have power because they have value,\u201d Abdul-Jabbar said. \u201cThe players that teams know that they can win with are going to be in a position to dictate what they want to do.\u201d And while few people would disagree with that, the fact that Davis\u2019 request went public \u2014 and the impact it had on the both the Pelicans and the Lakers, the team that appeared to go after the six-time All-Star the hardest before the trade deadline came and went earlier this month without a move being consummated \u2014 did not sit well with a number of the league\u2019s former players at All-Star weekend. And it isn\u2019t about the money. Top players like Davis, who will likely get his trade request fulfilled this summer are going to be well compensated one way or the other. But some think he might have been better served keeping it quiet until then. \u201cI just think it\u2019s a situation where they needed to keep it in house,\u201d Hall of Fame guard Rick Barry said. \u201cJust talk to the owners. Talk amongst yourselves. Airing your dirty laundry and putting stuff out there \u2026 I just don\u2019t understand why you want to get into a situation like that that does nobody any good and can only cause problems.\u201d Like Abdul-Jabbar, and like Davis, Barry also forced a trade. Back in his ABA days, he made it known that when the Washington Caps were moving to Norfolk, Virginia, he wanted no part of playing there. So Barry got traded to the New York Nets, the entire trade \u201csaga\u201d lasting no more than a week or two and all done during an offseason. Davis asking in-season, Barry said, had a negative effect on both the Pelicans and the Lakers. \u201cDoing it a year before, I don\u2019t understand,\u201d Barry said. \u201cHopefully they won\u2019t continue doing it that far in advance.\u201d Actually, that is nothing new. Kyrie Irving had two years, plus an option year, left on his deal with Cleveland when he asked for a trade and eventually got moved to the Boston Celtics . Paul George had a year left when he told Indiana that he wanted out . Both of those requests went public, and it could be argued that the Cavaliers and Pacers were ailed, at least somewhat, by losing leverage since it was no secret the superstars wanted to be moved. NBA Commissioner Adam Silver doesn\u2019t like trade demands, especially ones that go public. When the NBA adopted its most recent collective bargaining agreement, Silver said the notion was that teams would have the option to extend player deals a year early to avoid being blindsided by requests by those players to leave. It hasn\u2019t worked that way, with Davis just being the latest example. \u201cThe law of unintended consequences,\u201d Silver said. \u201cIt hasn\u2019t worked precisely as we had planned.\u201d Irving had a title with the Cavaliers. Kawhi Leonard had a championship with San Antonio when he asked to be moved , and ultimately got his way . George still doesn\u2019t have a championship, though flirted with one plenty of times when he was in Indiana only to be thwarted on annual basis by the Miami Heat. Davis doesn\u2019t have one. He hasn\u2019t been close. New Orleans went to the Western Conference semifinals last year, a great sign of progress. This year the Pelicans have plummeted back toward the bottom of the Western Conference. And Davis realizes that his window for winning and being elite won\u2019t last forever, so mindful of his legacy he wants to be moved. The great players are rich and going to be rich no matter where they play. The ring is also very much the thing, and Davis knows helping lead a team to a championship is vital to how he will be remembered. \u201cI just want to win,\u201d Davis said at All-Star weekend. The Pelicans haven\u2019t done enough of it, and this year was the wrong time for their winning percentage to fall off a cliff. So Davis made the ask, and Hall of Famer Dave Cowens said that\u2019s fine \u2014 as long as he accepts whatever comes next, whether it\u2019s good or bad. \u201cIf a player wants to usurp or influence a decision on personnel, then the accountability for that move if it doesn\u2019t work out, that\u2019s what it\u2019s about,\u201d Cowens said. \u201cYou can\u2019t have union and management doing the same things. \u2026 To me, it starts with the accountability. That\u2019s the biggest thing.\u201d Abdul-Jabbar said he understands why Davis\u2019 trade request is getting so much attention. It\u2019s because Davis \u2014 averaging 28 points and 13 rebounds this season \u2014 is worth it. \u201cThat\u2019s always going to be the case,\u201d Abdul-Jabbar said. \u201cThe most talented people out there in the job market are going to get the most attention.\u201d"},{"id":35463,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/powerrankings-2018-19-week-19","date":"2019-02-19","title":"Power Rankings, Week 19: Urgency rises for Lakers, others after All-Star break","content":" After an entertaining NBA All-Star 2019 in Charlotte and at least seven days off for all 30 teams, the season (which is already 70 percent complete) tips off again on Thursday, with much to be resolved in the next seven weeks. The last time James Harden scored fewer than 30 points, the Rockets were sitting at 12-14 and No. 14 in the Western Conference . The next game, Harden dropped 50 on the Lakers in a victory. Then he had 32 in the next game and 47 after that \u2026 and then 30-plus again and again until he stood alone with Wilt Chamberlain, who had previously owned the four-longest streaks. As we exit the All-Star break, Harden and Chamberlain are tied for second at 31 games ; Houston plays the Lakers on Thursday ( 10:30 ET, TNT ). Harden ran out of real estate this season on a chance to tie the all-time record \u2013 Wilt reached 65 straight in 1961-62 \u2013 but he stands to finish with the single-highest scoring average the league\u2019s seen since Michael Jordan\u2019s 37.1 ppg in 1986-87 . Harden also managed to find a widely lampooned boundary for the outer reaches of his patented step-back jumper: We all realized Giannis Antetokounmpo had made a jump last season, and that the Milwaukee Bucks, under new coach Mike Budenholzer, could be among the Eastern Conference contenders \u2014 especially with LeBron James moving out West . What maybe we didn\u2019t count on was Antetokounmpo taking it up another notch as Budenholzer and GM Jon Horst surrounded him with shooting, shooting and more shooting as they gave him full reign over the offense. Antetokounmpo has averaged an astounding 27.2 points (58.1 field goal percentage), 12.7 rebounds, six assists, 1.4 steals and 1.4 blocks per game. The Bucks are an NBA best 43-14 at the break, and Antetokounmpo is the current Kia MVP favorite . Also, he does things like this: The Toronto Raptors made a bold move before the season , sending DeMar DeRozan \u2014 the homegrown face of Toronto\u2019s franchise revival \u2014 to the San Antonio Spurs in a package that returned impending free-agent Kawhi Leonard, who played only nine games last season while dealing with a quad injury. Another season, another triple-double average for Oklahoma City star Russell Westbrook. And this time, it\u2019s not close: Westbrook, despite struggling to keep his shot north of 40 percent from the field, 25 percent from 3-point range and 65 percent from the line, is averaging 21.7 points, 11.2 rebounds and 11.2 assists per game. And he\u2019s done it while essentially deferring to Paul George as the team\u2019s No. 1 option \u2014 his usage rate (the percentage of his team\u2019s possessions used) is at its lowest mark since his second season. He has literally entered unprecedented territory, both with this third full season of statistical prowess and the still ongoing streak of 11 games with a triple-double . The previous record \u2014 held, of course, by Chamberlain \u2014 was 10. Russ had threatened several times in recent years, stringing together runs as long as seven games. Bolstered by the backcourt duo of speedy De\u2019Aaron Fox and sharpshooting Buddy Hield, the Kings have risen to 30-27, good for ninth in the super-competitive West \u2014 just four games back of No. 4 Portland. Either way, maybe not quite the time to be super confident as a fan of one of the other East contenders until you see the four Ls this spring. After a middling 10-point debut in Phoenix, Doncic rebounded to drop 26 points, six rebounds and three assists on the Timberwolves. For what it\u2019s worth, Young is actually coming along pretty well for Atlanta, who could be looking at a pair of Top-10 picks come June. But still. The highlight, without question, was a 50-point explosion on Halloween \u2014 a crucial career-high that Rose didn\u2019t seem ready to process. Out West, the unquestioned surprise at the top of the standings is the Denver Nuggets rising from a one-game playoff miss last season to a 39-18 mark, just two games behind the defending-champion Warriors. That\u2019s where once again we find the Golden State Warriors, owners of the last four conference banners, fully equipped to bring the heat in springtime again and make it five straight. > The East:  Five teams to watch come playoff time The issue, then, isn\u2019t whether the Warriors are monopolizing things. It\u2019s more about determining the identity of a potential Warriors slayer and the chances of such a team causing a seismic quake of an upset. * * * The discussion starts curiously enough with a team that didn\u2019t even make the playoffs last season. Losing on the final night of the 2017-18 season has served as a motivational face-slap for the Nuggets. They have seared through 2018-19 ever since, residing either at or near the penthouse in the West and desperately wanting to be taken seriously. For a team with a youthful core lacking in playoff experience, the Nuggets bring the swagger of a been-there, done-that contender and show plenty of staying power. They are a West-best 25-4 at home, but one of those rare losses came in a 31-point spanking the Warriors delivered on Jan. 15 that humbled the Nuggets at least temporarily. The Warriors did not, to paraphrase Nuggets coach Mike Malone, take that L on the way out the door. However, Denver still brings plenty to the table. They have more depth with the return of Isaiah Thomas, an All-Star center (Nikola Jokic) who runs the offense, a rising star in Jamal Murray and a drastically improved defense. Most importantly, they bring a sense that they belong in the mix. \u201cIf you don\u2019t want to give (respect) to us, so what, man? We don\u2019t care,\u201d Malone said. \u201c We \u2018re going to create our own respect. We\u2019re going to do what we do, and ultimately teams will take notice, people will take notice. I think you\u2019re starting to see that more and more.\u201d Jokic poses unique problems for the opposition. He\u2019s a quirky center, comfortable on the perimeter, where he\u2019s clever with back-door passes and is a semi-decent 3-point shooter (30.8 percent). He leads the NBA in post ups and uses his wide body to score in those situations, ranking third in post-up points . With the reduction of quality big men in the NBA, Jokic doesn\u2019t have a peer in terms of all-around skills \u2014 he\u2019s a triple-double threat \u2014 and the only West center with the defensive chops to make him work up a sweat is perhaps the Utah Jazz\u2019s Rudy Gobert. \u201cHe\u2019s got tricks, man,\u201d Oklahoma City Thunder guard Paul George said. \u201cIt goes with his nickname, the Joker. He keeps you on your toes and puts on a show every night he\u2019s out there.\u201d The Nuggets\u2019 flaw is experience and maybe top-shelf mental toughness. They\u2019re 14-14 on the road and only have Thomas and Paul Millsap as their most playoff-tested players. Overall, they\u2019ve never been thrown into the playoff fire. That\u2019s a significant disadvantage to take on against Golden State, especially if it should secure home-court advantage in a series. Houston is the wildest of wild cards. They were the Warriors\u2019 biggest threat last season, pushing them to (and falling in) Game 7 of the 2018 West finals . The Rockets began this season coping with key injuries and not so successfully at that, starting off 11-14, but have righted the ship since then. Chris Paul is back after missing 23 games and Clint Capela is scheduled to return from a thumb injury sometime this week. Plus, the Rockets added Kenneth Faried and Iman Shumpert in mid-season deals to bring more experience and depth. Of course, there\u2019s James Harden, who almost single-handedly lifted the Rockets during their injuries. The reigning Kia MVP has scored 30 or more points in 31 straight games to thrust himself back into the MVP conversation . But all that burn can wear on a player as the calendar flips from April to May. Will Harden still bring heavy minutes and big shots come May and June? And if not, will Paul\u2019s body \u2014 which betrayed him in the 2018 West finals \u2014 hold up to provide necessary support? \u201cI\u2019m just excited for the second half of the season, getting a full, healthy roster and taking it from there,\u201d Harden said. \u201cWe really haven\u2019t hit our stride yet as a team.\u201d As a contender, Oklahoma City is another strange one. They sport a virtually unchanged roster from last season\u2019s first-round loss to the Jazz , when George was 2-for-16 in the Game 6 ouster . OKC has since collected itself and so has George, 28, who finds himself a serious MVP contender as he enjoys a career season. Much has been made \u2014 and rightly so \u2014 about how Russell Westbrook has altered his game to benefit George. Here\u2019s Kevin Durant, of all people, on that dynamic: \u201cI think Paul is just going out there and playing free and understanding what his role is as a go-to scorer for the Thunder,\u201d Durant said. \u201cI think him and Russ have got some nice synergy out there along with their teammates. So, you\u2019re just starting to see him shine bright. I think he\u2019s always showed this stuff, but I think he has more opportunities to do so.\u201d Westbrook is averaging a triple-double yet again and has logged an NBA-record 11 straight triple-doubles (and counting). George has become OKC\u2019s savior in clutch moments, ranking seventh in total clutch points . This 1-2 punch is propelling the Thunder up the standings in the West, which makes their determining factor the help. Can Steven Adams, Jerami Grant and assorted others provide the proper mix of aid for OKC to make the Warriors notice? \u201cWe got a lot on this team right now,\u201d George said. \u201cI\u2019m not sure what\u2019s missing. Yes, we\u2019re not in The Finals and we\u2019re not in the playoffs yet. But what we\u2019ve got is enough. Me and Russ can shoulder it and we\u2019ve got enough support around us.\u201d There are plenty of imperfections among the rest of the field \u2014 the San Antonio Spurs, Los Angeles Lakers and the can-you-believe-it Sacramento Kings \u2014 but maybe the Jazz are better built for the postseason than any of them. Utah has two arguments in its favor: Defense and Donovan (Mitchell). That should be enough for the Jazz to again reach the semifinals and, if things break their way, the conference finals. Mitchell wasn\u2019t an All-Star in 2018-19, but will be someday. And he can get a jump on that support with another strong postseason. He\u2019s certainly capable of that, although after the first few months of the season, you had to wonder. He struggled with his shot and his command late in games. In addition, Utah was hurt by a difficult early schedule and didn\u2019t rise above .500 for good until Jan. 11. The good news for Utah is the schedule lightened up and Mitchell toughened up. His efficiency rate improved and his reliability returned, although opposing defenses are forcing him into attacking double teams or giving up the ball. They\u2019re wiser now and the Jazz still haven\u2019t found a solid secondary scorer. Gobert is their No. 2 scorer but he\u2019s more of a clean-up player who doesn\u2019t take volume shots. The Jazz aim to win with defense and intelligence. With Gobert among the league leaders in blocks and the Utah\u2019s defense back on track, the Jazz rank No. 4 in Defensive Rating (105.4 points per 100 possessions) . * * * To summarize, which of these four stands the best chance to come in second? Since anything\u2019s possible, we must rate the odds of one of them actually beating the Warriors. That puts the Nuggets and Rockets fairly even in that department, followed by the Thunder and Jazz. But make no mistake, for obvious reasons, there\u2019s an oceanic gap between that pack and the champs.  \u201cEvery year is a new challenge and different circumstances,\u201d Warriors star Stephen Curry said. \u201cBut make no mistake, we are motivated. We understand what\u2019s at stake.\u201d Three straight championships hasn\u2019t happened since the Shaquille O\u2019Neal-Kobe Bryant-led Lakers of the early 2000s . Four in five years is the stuff of legends, and so the Warriors are seeking a chance to reside with other legendary teams. Besides, with free agency beckoning this summer, there\u2019s no guarantee the fun times will continue much longer. Other than Draymond Green and Durant\u2019s dust-up and Curry\u2019s 11-game injury absence , Golden State has had few hiccups this season. Everyone on social media had fun with the former, until reality returned and the Warriors reclaimed their place in the NBA (for the regular season anyway). They\u2019re healthy now and, on some nights, look legendary. They have room to grow, with DeMarcus Cousins still getting his bearings. It\u2019s all good for the Warriors right now, and absent some unforeseen setback, how can they come up short for another Finals trip? You can argue that, with Cousins aboard, this is the strongest Warriors team in the Steve Kerr era. A championship must bear that out. Remember, the Warriors won an NBA-record 73 games in 2015-16 \u2026 only to become the first team to blow a 3-1 Finals lead . That ruined any argument of them delivering the greatest season in league history. One thing\u2019s for sure: Golden State isn\u2019t having sleepless nights over any team fighting for the right to deny them. \u201cBeing able to hoist that trophy at the end of the season, you can\u2019t put into words how much that means,\u201d said Warriors guard Klay Thompson. \u201cDoesn\u2019t matter who\u2019s standing across from us.\u201d * * * Shaun Powell has covered the NBA for more than 25 years. Dirk Nowitzki and Dwyane Wade will be linked forever , having battled twice in The Finals during their surefire Hall of Fame careers. Since they split  those meetings it\u2019s only fitting that these two living legends went out together in their final All-Star Game appearance. And they didn\u2019t disappoint. Dirk knocked down three deep 3-pointers for Team Giannis before halftime. Wade drained a 3-pointer of his own for Team LeBron before halftime. And he started the second half as Team LeBron rallied from a 13-point first-half deficit to take the lead at the end of the third quarter. Salute to two of the game\u2019s all-time greats. Stephen Curry\u2019s bounce pass. Giannis Antetokounmpo\u2019s head-at-the-rim-finish . Kevin Durant\u2019s reaction after being the victim of the dunk of the first half and perhaps the entire weekend. What was there not to love about a dunk that will forever be a part of All-Star Game lore? One of the most fascinating events during All-Star weekend every year is the Technology Summit, where the focus is on about basketball\u2019s future and the role of evolving technology. NBA Commissioner Adam Silver kicked things off Saturday morning by using an app on a phone to change the number and name on the back of a jersey, flipping it from a Kemba Walker model to a Stephen Curry model to a Michael Jordan model. The league\u2019s All-Stars gathered Sunday in Charlotte, N.C ., to put on a show at the Spectrum Center, only to see members of the two-time defending champions become the ringleaders once again. There was Steph Curry, raised in Charlotte and anxious to impress the old neighborhood, making the two prettiest bounce passes of the night, one to Giannis Antetokounmpo and one to \u2026 himself . There was Klay Thompson, wearing a different uniform than Curry for the first time in their careers. He was trying hard to bring trash-talking rights back to Oakland and came close to making a down payment. And there was Kevin Durant. He\u2019s the real MVP. All told, the 68th All-Star Game had some cold stretches and needed to be rescued, and \u2014 wouldn\u2019t you know \u2014 three members of the most decorated team this decade did what they do. It was super for entertainment value and dreadful for championship hopes held by anyone with ideas of tripping the Warriors come spring and summertime. At least the weekend wasn\u2019t a total Warriors romp: Curry did lose the MTN DEW 3-Point Contest to Joe Harris of the Brooklyn Nets. The All-Star weekend was a few years late coming to Charlotte, originally scheduled for 2017 prior to a politically charged delay , and the league hustled to do right by the city and also Michael Jordan, owner of the Hornets. The showcase gave the NBA some temporarily (and much-needed) relief from competition, not only the first two-thirds of the regular season, but also from the Anthony Davis sweepstakes . The centerpiece of the weekend was the game itself, and let the record show all of social media and the Los Angeles Lakers that LeBron James is indeed capable of picking players that can help him win. There was some question about that over the last few dramatic weeks. LeBron captained his team, perhaps notably containing four stars who\u2019ll become free agents this summer, to a 178-164 win over Team Giannis. The game was unique in that it contained 13 players on each squad instead of the usual 12. That\u2019s because Adam Silver used his commissioner\u2019s power to add two legends, Dwyane Wade and Dirk Nowitzki \u2014 one of whom is definitely retiring (Wade) and the other is expected to, but hasn\u2019t made anything official yet. When Team LeBron coach Mike Budenholzer sent Nowitzki to the scorer\u2019s table to check in, Mike Malone, not to be outcoached, immediately signaled for Wade. It was a staged photo-and-applause op and it worked; Wade and Dirk received standing ovations from the Spectrum Center as they jointly walked on the floor for the final time as All-Stars. What happened next was pure: Dirk hit his first three shots, all 3-pointers, as his teammates rose from the bench and celebrated each one. \u201cI just wanted to play a few minutes and hoist up a 3,\u201d he said. \u201cThe first shot I figured, \u2018Hey, last time on stage, I\u2019m going to go for it,\u2019 and it went in. The second one, I said, \u2018I\u2019ll get a little deeper,\u2019 and it went in. The third, I wanted to see what happened and it went in too. It was a pleasure to compete one more time with these guys. A great weekend for me.\u201d Shortly thereafter, Wade connected with his BFF and former teammate LeBron on a few lob passes, reminiscent of their winning combinations on a pair of championships in Miami. \u201cLike I\u2019ve been saying the last couple of days, it\u2019s been a bittersweet moment for me and him,\u201d LeBron said. \u201cThe bitter part is obviously this being the last time on the same floor together and the memories we have as competitors and teammates. \u201cAnd then the sweet part of it is seeing him be able to go out on his own terms, saying when he\u2019s done and nobody forcing him out and or anything of that nature. He\u2019s able to hang it up when he wants to hang it up and be at peace with it.\u201d It was fun and fitting and the two future Hall of Famers were clearly affected and choked up, especially as they accepted framed All-Star jerseys during a brief ceremony prior to the fourth quarter. But make no mistake, this was more about the Warriors here at a critical checkpoint, flexing their talent for all to see and envy and ultimately respect. Thompson found himself in a playful one-upmanship with Curry and, well \u2026 Thompson came up short. He did drill a 3-pointer from the corner, while Curry, sitting nearby on the bench, yelled for a miss. But Curry dropped a deep 3-pointer while being hacked by Thompson, falling to the floor at the feet of rapper Quavo and then completing the 4-point play. \u201cIt was good to see Steph knock down that shot over Klay because Klay is always talking trash to him,\u201d said Durant. \u201cIt was fun to see. Those guys are always joking around and seeing who can make the most shots. Their chemistry together is second-to-none. So we know we\u2019re going to be talking about that play for the next two days.\u201d Durant snagged his second All-Star Game MVP, and first with the Warriors, by tallying 31 points, including some big buckets down the stretch. There isn\u2019t a major trophy Durant hasn\u2019t won: two Finals MVPs, two All-Star MVPs, a regular-season MVP, two NBA titles. His next might be another title this summer, and after that it\u2019s time for a new contract \u2026 somewhere. For Curry, the weekend was a dream. It was 27 years ago that he watched his first All-Star Weekend from the lap of his father, who was a 3-Point Contest participant in 1992. He came from humble basketball beginnings, a scrawny teenager who couldn\u2019t draw much interest from Division I schools, and then took nearby Davidson College to national prominence. The entire Curry family soaked it all in: Steph, Dell, brother Seth \u2014 who battled his brother in the 3-Point Contest \u2014 and the rest. Appearing in Charlotte for the All-Star Game served as a career highlight to be checked off a rather long and growing list for Curry. Feeling a bit pressured to perform, especially after being upset in the 3-Point Contest Finals, Curry unloaded with a pair of plays made for YouTube. On the break, he bounced the ball off the floor and high in the air, thereby qualifying as a lob pass, which was dunked by Giannis. \u201cI think that pass was going to Joel (Embiid) but I was able to sneak in there and make it look like a good pass to me,\u201d Giannis said. \u201cIt was a nice play.\u201d And then, with the clock ticking off the final seconds of Charlotte\u2019s basketball weekend, Curry bounced another pass high, grabbed it, twisted in the air, and dunked a reverse. \u201cAll y\u2019all saw me in LA a couple of weeks ago\u201d said Curry, making mention of his embarrassing slip and fall while attempting a fancy breakaway dunk against the Clippers. \u201cWell, I redeemed myself.\u201d With that, the game and weekend were wrapped for Charlotte, by a kid from Charlotte. Everybody go home. Everybody prepare for the season\u2019s last two months. And more of what\u2019s coming from the Warriors. * * * Shaun Powell has covered the NBA for more than 25 years. Uniquely enough, that 3-year-old was himself. Back in his hometown for All-Star weekend, Curry sat courtside after participating in the MTN DEW 3-point contest with a jacket that was similar in style \u2014 and obviously larger in size \u2014 to the one he donned on All-Star Saturday Night as a kid. The original photograph was taken in 1992 when Stephen sat courtside with his father Dell Curry, a former sharpshooter for the Charlotte Hornets who had also just participated in the 3-point contest. The event was held in Orlando that year. Dell was back in front of the Charlotte crowd to kick off the 2019 3-point contest with some of his old teammates. He and the former All-Stars didn\u2019t exactly light it up , but they raised $35,000 for charity. Once the official competition began, Dell watched as his sons Steph and Seth battled for the trophy. While a victory would have been special for the Curry family, the oldest son and six-time All-Star was still able to bring things full circle."},{"id":35456,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/adam-silver-presser-column","date":"2019-02-17","title":"NBA Commissioner addresses trade requests and more at All-Star press conference","content":" CHARLOTTE, N.C. \u2014 Not all media attention is good media attention, NBA commissioner Adam Silver confirmed Saturday at his annual All-Star Weekend news conference. Don\u2019t get it twisted, the NBA relishes the idea that it can dominate news cycles and sports chatter across 12 months. The idea that free agency, roster maneuvers, trade deadlines, buyout markets, summertime player development and even rumors and gossip can keep tongues wagging and ratings high has been widely embraced at league headquarters and by its member teams. But that doesn\u2019t mean all of its business should be conducted in the street. What the NBA, the New Orleans Pelicans, All-NBA center Anthony Davis, his agent Rich Paul and the Los Angeles Lakers have been embroiled in over the past three weeks would have been better handled \u201cbehind closed doors,\u201d the commissioner told reporters at Spectrum Center in the hour before State Farm All-Star Saturday Night. \u201cWhen they make a public spectacle of it,\u201d Silver said, \u201cI hear you in terms of the enormous media interest that comes from it. But that\u2019s not the kind of media interest we\u2019re looking for.\u201d Paul notified the Pelicans near the end of January that Davis would not sign a contract extension and preferred to be traded to a championship contender. He didn\u2019t just tell the Pelicans, though; he went public, less than two weeks before the Feb. 7 trade deadline. The league fined Davis $50,000 for violating a rule in the collective bargaining agreement prohibiting players or their representatives from making public trade demands. The plot was thick from the start because Paul\u2019s biggest client is LeBron James, giving the instant perception that James and the Lakers were trying to leverage Davis to them. From there, a series of nasty dominoes fell: Paul issued a list of four preferred destinations . Davis\u2019 father publicly tried to thwart Boston\u2019s interest. The Pelicans declined to cut a deal with L.A. \u2013 and got accused of intentionally trying to stir discord within the Lakers\u2019 locker room by allegedly leaking players\u2019 names. Once the deadline passed, the NBA reportedly reminded New Orleans that sitting out Davis \u2013 to protect its asset until the offseason by avoiding potential injury \u2013 was not an acceptable tactic, even as the team seems committed to losing for draft-lottery position. It all led to Friday, when Pelicans GM Dell Demps, who held the line against the Lakers\u2019 overtures, was fired . All of that is the sort of chaos, and headlines, the NBA would prefer to avoid. \u201cWhether it be a team or a player not meeting a contractual obligation,\u201d Silver said, \u201cthat\u2019s something you just don\u2019t want to see as a league.\u201d While Davis had 18 months left on his New Orleans contract before he could become a free agent, Silver noted that current CBA is structured to encourage players and their teams to address such stalemates a year in advance. In this case, it would have been fine for Davis and Paul to notify the Pelicans this summer that the All-Star would not re-sign in 2020, thereby giving the team time to probe trades in an orderly fashion. That\u2019s where the closed doors matter. Just in the past two years, Paul George, Kyrie Irving, Kawhi Leonard, Jimmy Butler, Davis and Kristaps Porzingis have gone public while under contract with trade requests, to varying levels of disruption to their teams. Silver acknowledged that teams can \u201cblindside\u201d players by abruptly trading them, such as occurred last season with Blake Griffin and DeMar DeRozan. But loyalty isn\u2019t the same thing as a guaranteed contract; no-trade clauses, while rare, can be negotiated. The NBA, under both Silver and his predecessor David Stern, has long been committed to player movement via free agency. But players forcing their way out, in a desire to land in destination markets for basketball or even outside business reasons, can affect the balance of power in the league and the ability of less popular markets to compete. \u201cI don\u2019t want to be overly defensive here because I don\u2019t want to defend a system that is \u2018smoothly operating,\u2019\u201d Silver said. \u201cI believe it\u2019s an area where we can do better. Something we have to sit down with the players\u2019 association. \u201cBut I\u2019m ultimately confident that these are not endemic problems with the league. To me, these are very fixable issues.\u201d Silver fielded questions on topics both related and unrelated to the recent trade demands\/tampering controversy, including: He said it\u2019s too soon to know if the league\u2019s changes to the draft-lottery \u2014 flattening the odds of landing the No. 1 pick to 14.0 percent each for the three losingest clubs \u2014 will have the desired effect of discouraging \u201ctanking.\u201d Four NBA teams entered the All-Star break on pace to win 20 games or fewer this season. Silver does not believe a race to the bottom is in either the league\u2019s or those teams\u2019 best interest. Especially when franchises do it for multiple years. \u201cI understand genuine rebuilding,\u201d he said. But the idea that, if you\u2019re going to be bad, you might as well be really bad? Said Silver: \u201cI believe, personally, that\u2019s corrosive for those organizations.\u201d As encouraging as the current standings might be \u2014 with teams in Milwaukee, Denver, Oklahoma City and Indiana thriving \u2014 Silver sees payroll issues as potentially undermining competitive balance. Some teams have more money to spend, others chose to spend to the point of unprofitability. He noted that the NBA has had seven different champions over the past 11 Finals, while the NFL \u2014 known for its parity \u2014 has seen New England play in nine of the past 18 Super Bowls. Asked about the Dallas Mavericks\u2019 front-office sexual harassment and discrimination scandal that grabbed headlines almost a year ago, Silver said the team\u2019s and the league\u2019s follow-up has generated results. \u201cWhat was reported to me and through the organization was that there was a complete sea change in culture on the business side of the Mavericks,\u201d he said. Silver recently traveled to Dallas and spoke with employees. The idea to invite aging legends Dirk Nowitzki and Dwyane Wade to the All-Star Game, adding a roster spot for each, came from a fan\u2019s e-mail, the commissioner said. Silver called the Currys \u2014 father Dell and sons Steph and Seth \u2014 the \u201cfirst family of Charlotte, at least this week.\u201d Dell Curry played for the Hornets, with All-Star Steph and fellow 3-point contestant Seth raised in the area. Silver provided background on the shift of Charlotte\u2019s All-Star Weekend from 2017 to 2019, the NBA\u2019s response to a political battle in North Carolina that critics said discriminated against members of the LGBTQ community. He credited Hornets owner Michael Jordan, team president Fred Whitfield and others with helping to get the controversial HB2 bill repealed and bringing together those on both sides to restore the game. This is something I\u2019ll never forget.\u201d \u2014 Shaun Powell When Giannis Antetokounmpo was toiling in an obscure Greek league as a teenager, he wasn\u2019t sure exactly where his basketball dreams were headed. But the sweet moment is that we\u2019ve got so much more life to live together, and we will continue that.\u201d \u2014 Jonathan Hartzell The Beard begat the Narrative, which at this point in James Harden\u2019s season reads something like this: Harden is a remarkably prolific offensive player, with an array of moves, a deft shooting touch and the strength to create space where none existed. But the way he pounds the ball, dribbling and probing until deep into the shot clock, makes him a player whose games aren\u2019t that fun to watch and whose style might not attract teammates with talents and ambitions of their own. \u201cGo ask those guys how many of them would like to play with [Harden],\u201d NBA Hall of Famer Rick Barry said as All-Star Weekend started. In what by design is a sport in which all players are available to touch the basketball, Harden\u2019s Houston Rockets are a 1 + 4 proposition. The league\u2019s leading scorer (36.6 ppg) also leads in usage rate (40.3), an estimated percentage of a team\u2019s plays a player uses while on the floor. That\u2019s second-highest since the advanced stat started to be tracked in 1977-78, behind only Russell Westbrook\u2019s 41.65 two years ago. Harden came into the schedule break with an active string of consecutive 30-point games that stretches back 31 games now. He leads the NBA in free throw attempts, which means more plays end with the ball in his hands when whistled than anyone else\u2019s. And more than 300 of his league-high 561 field goals have come without assists, further evidence of limited ball movement. As former 3-point marksman turned TNT broadcaster Dennis Scott wondered, \u201cTo play with a guy who dribbles 40 times a possession and has more than 300 baskets that weren\u2019t assisted? That would be tough. \u201cThey\u2019re winning. Guys seem to be saying the right things. He and Chris Paul are doing the \u2018your turn, my turn\u2019 pick-and-roll. Members of Team LeBron will get their chance to play with Harden Sunday (if they haven\u2019t already had it) and weren\u2019t inclined to be critical. He\u2019s one of the best players in the world, so you just adapt to the way he plays.\u201d Milwaukee\u2019s Khris Middleton already plays with a ball-centric teammate in Giannis Antetokounmpo, though the Greek Freak\u2019s usage rate (31.9) represents 20 percent less ball dominance than Harden. Contrary to the Rockets star\u2019s tempo, Antetokounmpo tends to attack the defense hard early in a possession, then find an open teammate on the perimeter. He\u2019s not overthinking things. He\u2019s just playing. Things just flow much easier for him now, having that year under his belt with familiarity with Kenny, the system, all of that.\u201d \u2014 John Schuhmann Buddy Hield is having a breakout season for the surprisingly relevant Sacramento Kings, averaging 20.5 points and ranking fourth in the league in 3-point percentage at 44.9 percent. Hield was already one of the league\u2019s best catch-and-shoot guys. Last season, he shot 50.2 percent on catch-and-shoot threes, the best mark among 94 players who attempted at least 200. This year, Hield has made 47.3 percent of his catch-and-shoot 3-pointers, the third best mark among 99 players who have attempted at least 150 through Thursday. Where Hield has seen an improvement is in his shooting off the dribble. Last season, Hield shot 35.9 percent on 2.1 pull-up 3-point attempts per game, a mark which ranked 25th among 55 players who attempted at least 100 pull-up threes. This season, Hield has shot 40.3 percent on 2.6 pull-up 3-point attempts per game, and the only players who have shot better on at least 100 pull-up attempts are four All-Stars and Orlando\u2019s Terrence Ross. Being a 40-percent 3-point shooter off the dribble is what gets defenses to adjust their schemes. It can open other things up for both Hield and his teammates. It\u2019s obviously something that Hield has worked on, and he\u2019s also got more license to shoot quickly in the fast-paced offense that the Kings have been playing this season. Hield said that the way the Kings are running is playing to the strengths of him and his teammates. That means Hornets guard Kemba Walker might be ready for his close-up. Fifteen times in the 67 NBA All-Star Games \u2014 a success rate of 22.4 percent \u2014 a player performing on his home court has been named MVP. There\u2019s the built-in advantage of familiar surroundings, including the floor, the rims and shooting backgrounds. A diverse group of fans, while not necessarily from Charlotte in this case, still look for easy hooks when it\u2019s time to cheer. All-Star teammates often try to make the local guy look good, too. As for Walker, this will be his third consecutive All-Star appearance, so he should be past any jitters. If he stars Sunday, he\u2019ll be doing it against the best competition in the world. Working against Walker\u2019s MVP chances, perhaps? The trend of host city All-Star MVPs has cooled, with only four players doing it in the past 26 years: Anthony Davis in New Orleans in 2017, Kobe Bryant in L.A. in 2011, Shaquille O\u2019Neal (as co-MVP with Bryant) in Phoenix in 2009 and O\u2019Neal in L.A. in 2004. Also, betting odds out of Las Vegas favor Team LeBron to win the game by 5.5 points. And while Antetokounmpo is listed as a slight favorite over James for the MVP trophy, Walker and the Greek Freak both would have to buck a trend if the game\u2019s line is accurate. (AP) \u2014 The NBA is bringing a pro league to Africa. The Basketball Africa League, a new collaboration between the NBA and the sport\u2019s global governing body FIBA, was announced Saturday. The initial plan is for the 12-team league to begin play in January, and former President Barack Obama is among those who are expected to have direct involvement with the league\u2019s operations. It\u2019s yet to be determined which existing club teams will be part of the league. Qualification tournaments will be held later this year to determine those clubs, with teams from Angola, Egypt, Kenya, Morocco, Nigeria, Rwanda, Senegal, South Africa and Tunisia expected to be among those taking part. No nation will have more than two teams in the league. \u201cAs we\u2019ve been talking about this concept over the last several months, there\u2019s been a tremendous reception from several of our NBA team owners,\u201d Silver said. \u201cSeveral of our partners have also expressed an interest to work with us in Africa.\u201d Silver said Pepsi and Nike\u2019s Jordan Brand are among the partners who have reached out to the NBA and said they want to be part of the Africa league. Silver also said that Obama \u2014 an enormous basketball fan \u2014 has told him he wants to have a direct role in the league, the specifics of which have yet to be determined. \u201cThere\u2019s been a fantastic reception,\u201d Silver said. Obama spoke on a video that was shown during the event where Silver announced the league. \u201cThrough sport, if you put in effort, you will be rewarded,\u201d Obama said. The NBA and FIBA\u2019s involvement will include financial support and resources toward continued growing of the game on the continent, as well as providing training for players, coaches and referees and some infrastructure for the new league. Silver said there are more than 400 companies in Africa that generate more than $1 billion annually, but that sport there has not seen the same growth \u2014 yet. \u201cAfrica has a huge economic engine,\u201d Silver said. The NBA has held three games in Africa since 2015, all of them selling out \u2014 two games in Johannesburg, the other in Pretoria. Many of the league\u2019s current players and coaches, along with several legends and Hall of Famers, have been part of those trips. \u201cI went with them last year,\u201d Basketball Hall of Famer Kareem Abdul-Jabbar said. \u201cThe NBA reaches out across the world.\u201d The league has an office in South Africa, has helped create 87 learn-and-play facilities in seven African nations, and 13 players who were born in Africa on opening-night NBA rosters this season. The league also built an academy in Senegal that opened nearly two years ago. \u201cIt\u2019s a huge joy to see our partnership with the NBA enter unchartered territory as we work together for the first time to maximize the potential of professional basketball in Africa,\u201d said Andreas Zagklis, FIBA\u2019s secretary general. This marks the first time the NBA has been involved with the operation of a league outside of North America. \u201cWe\u2019re excited to work closely with the NBA to develop and put in a place a professional league like none that we have ever seen in our region before,\u201d said FIBA Africa Executive Director Alphonse Bile. \u201cThrough the Basketball Africa League, we can provide the many great clubs and players with the best possible environment to compete for the highest stakes.\u201d The NBA says more details about the new league will be released in the coming months."},{"id":46524,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/charlotte-hornets-kemba-walker-represents-well-faces-decision","date":"2019-02-16","title":"All-Star starter Kemba Walker at home in Charlotte, hopes to stay","content":" CHARLOTTE, N.C. \u2014 Long after his playing days ended, his presence still seems everlasting and omnipresent, rising above the state that raised him and especially here in the city that worships him. Michael Jordan remains the dominant basketball symbol in Charlotte, the jump man with legs that still soar and straddle, and that\u2019s precisely the problem for the team he owns. Because the Hornets, mostly uninspiring on his watch, have long searched for a player compelling enough to put a different face on the franchise. Well, for one day at least, someone else will rep the Hornets and hear the applause and win the crowd and in some ways become bigger than the boss. And when this happens, during the introductions of the starting lineup Sunday at the 68th NBA All-Star Game (8 ET, On TNT, coverage begins at 7) , right in the arena that Jordan Built, Kemba Walker will execute an expression that Jordan made famous and \u2026 shrug. \u201cPeople think of the Charlotte Hornets and they think of me,\u201d said Walker, shaking his head. \u201cIt\u2019s kind of mind blowing to me as well.\u201d Getting the annual midseason showpiece awarded to Charlotte was an accomplishment for Jordan, who\u2019s generally recognized as the game\u2019s greatest player. Yet having one of the Hornets get voted a starting guard for Team Giannis is more gratifying for Jordan the executive and team owner. Walker serves as Jordan\u2019s opus, one of the few decisions the Franchise Got Right, a fun-to-watch little guy who has carried the club the last few years by raising his game and shedding his flaws. The ascent of Walker does come with fine print, however. The time left on his contract expires at season\u2019s end and Walker, still in his prime at 28, will be free to walk to rosier pastures if he so chooses. It will take Jordan\u2019s persuasive power, along with a chunk of money, to convince Walker that Charlotte remains the place for him. This is Walker\u2019s third All-Star trip, first as a starter, and he\u2019s only the Hornets\u2019 second All-Star since Jordan took control of the team in 2010. Charlotte couldn\u2019t have a more ideal representative as a host. Walker is gracious, humble and friendly, easily a fan favorite because of that along with his talent, a package that reflects well on the Hornets. \u201cHaving Kemba as an All-Star gives me great pleasure because I always believed this kid was an All-Star, and he has proven that three years in a row and this year by being a starter,\u201d Jordan said the other day. \u201cI always thought there was something special about this kid.\u201d This is a breakout season for Walker, placing him near the top shelf among guards: Career highs in scoring (24.9), rebounds (4.4) and tying his career high in assists at 5.6. He\u2019s made himself a more efficient three-point shooter and now registers around 38 percent. Bringing quickness off the dribble and a precise step-back jumper, he has taken over games and bailed out the Hornets countless times. He dropped a career-high 60 points on the Sixers, torched the Wizards for 47, punished the Celtics with 43. He takes 20 shots a game, eight more than the next highest Hornet, yet there\u2019s little in Walker\u2019s game that hints of selfishness, and he\u2019s respected in the locker room. \u201cHe\u2019s just a good guy and everyone gravitates towards him,\u201d said forward Marvin Williams. \u201cHe comes to play every night and works hard. There\u2019s nothing not to like.\u201d The feeling is mutual with Walker. Born and raised in the shadow of New York City, he feels at peace in Charlotte and the slower pace and among people who keep him grounded. That\u2019s why Charlotte is his year-round home and he recently purchased a large plot of land to build another. \u201cThey\u2019ve supported me through a lot of bad times; they could\u2019ve given up on my early in my career when I was playing through my mistakes,\u201d Walker said. \u201cWe\u2019re not one of those teams in the playoffs every year so it could be easy to lose interest in a team or a player but it hasn\u2019t been like that. This community, the fans, they\u2019ve been really supportive of me.\u201d Suddenly, the city had an athlete big enough to share the podium with quarterback Cam Newton of the Carolina Panthers, a frequent presence in the front row at Spectrum Center. \u201cCam and I came in the same year,\u201d Walker said. \u201cWe were both with the same shoe company at one point. Lived in the same building when we first got here. Cam is a great dude and basketball fan. Great role model for this community. Both of us got better every season. He\u2019s an MVP of his league and it\u2019s been fun to watch his growth over the years. We\u2019ve both have had huge effects on this city and it\u2019s good to know that.\u201d The Hornets took Walker in ninth in the 2011 draft, a place of misery for the franchise. In 15 drafts since the Hornets were reborn in Charlotte, Walker is the only player to reach All-Star status. Others either didn\u2019t last long or made only modest impressions: Adam Morrison, Emeka Okafor, Raymond Felton, DJ Augustin, Gerald Henderson, Michael-Kidd Gilchrist, Cody Zeller, Frank Kaminsky. That\u2019s why the Hornets have made the playoffs only three times and never made the second round. Walker gradually sharpened his decision-making and stretched his shooting range and improved on the skills that won him a national championship at UConn. \u201cMichael drafted me,\u201d Walker said. \u201cWhen that happened, the first thing that went through my mind is this guy is giving me an opportunity. So I\u2019m going to give it everything I got. That\u2019s what I do for MJ, ever since I\u2019ve been here, each and every night. To try to play the game the right way. Play hard. And a lot has to do with him.\u201d Walker\u2019s allegiance to Jordan will be tested in July when the guard becomes a free agent. It\u2019s a potentially complicated situation. For the past four years the Hornets had Walker at a bargain; right now he\u2019s their sixth highest-paid player at $12 million. He\u2019s the lowest-paid All-Star starter by $8 million. Meanwhile, the Hornets\u2019 salary cap is swollen with pricey players whose production hasn\u2019t matched their salaries. As a result, the Hornets could be in a financial pickle this summer. If Walker makes All-NBA this season, he can command a five-year, $221 million \u201csupermax\u201d contract from the Hornets. If he\u2019s not All-NBA, his Hornets\u2019 money ceiling is five years and $189 million. Another team can offer $140 million over six; the hometown Knicks, among others, have cash. If the Hornets do give Walker the max, they risk a great chance of paying the luxury tax next season, a steep price for a middle of the road, small market team. \u201cIt will be very important to keep him,\u201d said Muggsy Bogues, one of the original Hornets. \u201cHopefully they can, but it will be challenging because giving him a max and not being able to improve the team is something they\u2019re going to be looking at. I know the priority is that he\u2019s here. I cannot see any scenario where he\u2019s not in a Hornets\u2019 uniform next year.\u201d About his upcoming decision, Walker said: \u201cI don\u2019t even know yet. I just want to get to the playoffs and when the summer comes I want to make the right decision for me and my family. I\u2019ve never been a free agent, so I don\u2019t know what to expect yet.\u201d It bodes well for the Hornets that Walker never made a trade demand or expressed any public distaste for the franchise unlike Paul George and Anthony Davis and Kawhi Leonard, stars who became disenchanted as free agency approached. Walker would have good reason; even now the Hornets aren\u2019t a lock for the playoffs this year and lack ample assets besides Walker to make a drastic improvement next season. \u201cPeople go through tough times that\u2019s how I\u2019ve taken it,\u201d Walker said. \u201cI always felt like I\u2019ve grown because of it. I never let it bother me or stop me from becoming a good player. I could\u2019ve easily done that or asked for a trade. I want to build something here. I want to try and make us one of the top teams one day. I love this place. I want to help take this organization to places it has never been.\u201d He has a message for any player at the All-Star Game seeking to recruit him: \u201cFor me, I love competing. I love playing against these other players, the great players. I don\u2019t want to go join their teams. If any want to come play on my team, I\u2019m good with that. But I\u2019m a competitor. Playing against these guys drives me and fuels me. \u201cThere\u2019s something to be said for being on a team for your whole career. Not many players have done that. Only a select few. That\u2019s a goal to accomplish.\u201d Sounds like he\u2019s receptive to staying if the money is right. Until then, there\u2019s a city to represent, a franchise flag to carry and large spotlight awaiting Walker when the All-Star Game begins Sunday in this town. His town. The Spectrum Center will be flush with LeBron James, Kevin Durant, the retiring Dirk Nowitizki and Dwyane Wade and of course Steph Curry, born and raised in Charlotte. There will also be a familiar face at courtside in the form of Michael Jordan. All bring bigger profiles than a certain 6-1 guard for Team Giannis. Kemba Walker will be on his floor, though, and therefore will feel right at home. That\u2019s a good sign for the All-Star Game today, and maybe for the Hornets tomorrow. * * * Shaun Powell has covered the NBA for more than 25 years. The topic of the Houston guard and his confounding, tantalizing, vexing ways with the basketball came up during a referees roundtable discussion Friday afternoon at All-Star Weekend. Three executives who oversee NBA officials met with a small group of reporters: Byron Spruell, president of league operations; Michelle Johnson, senior vice president and head of referee operations, and Monty McCutchen, the longtime game official now working as VP, head of referee development and training. The purpose? To have an informal state-of-the-season discussion, review certain \u201cpoints of education\u201d identified at the start of 2018-19 (such as \u201cfreedom of movement\u201d guidelines) and field a few questions. It was in that context that McCutchen was asked about Harden and his many moves, some of which appear to bleed into offensive fouls or run astray of other rules, such as traveling. McCutchen, who prefers not to talk publicly about individual players, instead use the platform to discuss how referees try to apply a standard framework in which all players, in all their individual styles, can thrive. \u201cWe cannot target players,\u201d McCutchen said, noting that he and other supervisors will talk to referees about player types. \u201cJames is not the only player who does that, and I don\u2019t want to go into every player who has a bag of tricks. \u201cOur rule book doesn\u2019t support me getting inside a player\u2019s head and saying, \u2018Well, he\u2019s trying to manipulate something.\u2019 I have a physical act that took place based on the principles of our rule book. And those standards are set up so that within those rules, people can play the game that they see fit.\u201d The real test comes when an innovative player introduces something different from what officials are used to. One example McCutchen gave was the willingness of ball handlers to expose tue basketball to a defender\u2019s reach. Instead of shielding the ball, per old school tactics, many current players have enough hand strength to hold the ball in front, enticing their opponents to reach and risk rip-move fouls of them, enticing defenders to reach for it and make themselves vulnerable to rip-move fouls. \u201cHow can I sit there and say, \u2018That\u2019s not good basketball?\u2019 McCutchen said. \u201cShaquille [O\u2019Neal] was another example. We never had a 7-foot-1, 295-pound man who had 2-percent body fat who could do the things Shaquille could do. That put pressure on you [as a referee].\u201d The league\u2019s leading scorer at 36.6 points per game, Harden has been on a tear not seen in the NBA since the early prime of Michael Jordan or, perhaps, the way-back days of Wilt Chamberlain. In his last game before the All-Star break, he scored 42 points against Minnesota to push his streak of scoring 30 or more points to 31 games. That tied Chamberlain for the second-longest in league history (Chamberlain also hold the record of 65 such games). Harden\u2019s most challenging bit of trickery is his step-back 3-pointer, which sometimes results in a traveling violation and sometimes does not. What McCutchen wanted people to know, at least, was that no new rules have been written legislating for or against that move. \u201cIt\u2019s not a new rule,\u201d the former NBA ref said, again not focusing on Harden specifically. \u201cIt\u2019s always been that you gathered the ball and you took two steps to the rim. But nowhere in our rule book does it say that has to be forward. Innovation says, \u2018I can take two steps backwards.\u2019 \u201cNow here\u2019s the problem: Sometimes the feet aren\u2019t quite right. The rhythm\u2019s not quite right on that move. So now I\u2019ve got to get that little baby step in. That\u2019s where it becomes difficult, because I\u2019m also refereeing whether said player is being fouled or not.\u201d As players innovate, referees have to react and adapt. Said McCutchen: \u201cWhat we\u2019re exploring right now is how do we tweak our mechanics so that our teamwork can keep up with the innovations?\u201d McCutchen talked at length about referees striving for consistency across all 48 minutes of a game, and being as ready and willing in the final seconds to call a supposed minor violation such as traveling as they would any other foul. In the process, he shed light on the emphasis officials have put on traveling violations this season. Per data collected by the league, he said, \u201can inordinate amount of defensive fouls come after those few traveling calls that are missed.\u201d * * * Steve Aschburner has written about the NBA since 1980.
